Two Tips to save some time on the Last Day Revision:
1. At some places we have also given Derivations & Proofs for initial conceptual understanding. These needs to be
skipped on the last day revision. Please exercise your discretion.
2. Make an Audio podcast during your last month revision for ~20 to 30 questions in your own voice for such questions
that you feel are easy & doesn't require reading & solving entire Q on the last day. For those questions, listen your own
audio podcast on last day revision.

Concepts have been connected by matching colors to achieve clearer understanding of such Concepts and to increase your
revision speed by 2x.

EPS
$=\frac{EAES}{n}or\frac{EAT^{*}}{n}$ *If Pref shares doesn't exist
Dividend %
$=\frac{DPS}{Face~value}$
vs Dividend Yield % vs Dividend Payout Ratio
$=\frac{DPS}{MP}$
PE Ratio (Price Earnings Ratio)
Retention Ratio
$=\frac{EPS-DPS}{EPS}$ or 1 - DPR
$=\frac{DPS}{EPS}$
Earnings Yield %
Observe that PER and Earnings Yield%
have inverse relationship
$=\frac{MP}{EPS}$
 Accordingly, $MP=PER\times EPS$
Interpretation of PE Ratio
$=\frac{tPS}{MP}$
✓ A Co. having higher goodwill, brand name & reputation enjoys higher PE Ratio eg HUL, Nestle etc.
✓ A Co. perceived less risky by investors will command higher PE Ratio.
A Co. whose future growth expectations are higher will have higher PE Ratio.
✓ All things being constant, a Co. whose PE Ratio is higher is Overvalued and a Co. whose PE Ratio is
lower is Undervalued.

year 1 to n, then we get PV at yr 0. On the same analogy, if we put amount from yr 5 to n, then
we'll get PV at the end of yr 4.

Swap Ratio/ Exchange Ratio
& Total Number of Shares Outstanding after Merger

Hint: No. of Shares issued to target (An)
... Total no. of sh $O/s$
625000
600000
$=300000\times\frac{3}{4}=225000$
$=n+\Delta n=400000+225000=625000$
Swap Ratio means "How many shares of Acquiror will be issued against every 1 share of Target
Company" So, 3:4 means 0.75 shares of acquiror will be issued against every 1 share of Target.
Don't read Swap Ratio of 3:4 as "3 is to 4"
Correct Approach is to read ":" symbol as "for", hence Swap Ratio is "3 for 4" meaning 3 new
shares of Acquiror will be issued for every 4 shares of Target or 0.75 for every 1.
Synergy
means "Excess amount over and above the simple summation of the two numbers." Synergy could be
either in Earnings or in Market Value or Both.
Synergy in Earnings $=E_{AT}-(E_{A}+E_{T})$  Synergy in Market Value $=V_{AT}-(V_{A}+V_{T})$
here, A means Acquiror, Tmeans Target & AT means Merged firm

What should be the Share Exchange Ratio ?
Maximum Swap Ratio (always from the point of view of Acquiror)
Concept: 100% of Synergy gains shall accrue to the Target & no synergy gains to acquirer.
Hence, Post-merger EPS or MP should be set equal to Acquiror's Pre-merger EPS or MP.
Based on Earnings
Max Swap
=
Ratio
Revised EPS (including whole
Synergy in earnings)
EPSA
Based on Market Value
Revised $MP_{T}$ (including whole
value)
$Max~Swap_{Ratio}=\frac{Synergy~in~mark}{MP_{A}}$
Refer bottom of the page for Tabular format to calc Max SR
Swap Ratio formula
Relevant factor of Target firm
Swap ratio = Relevant factor of Acquiror firm
!
Caution
Notes
1.
2.
here, Relevant factor means any factor (say
EPS, MP, BVPS etc.) that needs to be
maintained or a factor based on which swap
ratio needs to be calculated
Do not make the mistake of using Total data (eg. Total earnings, Total M. cap, Total
Book Value etc.) in SR formula. Always use per share data (eg. EPS, MP, BVPS) in Swap
Ratio Formula
When SR is based on some negative parameters / ratios (where lower number of such
ratios are considered better over higher numbers eg. gross NPA ratio, Debt Equity
ratio etc. are lower the better) then formula to calc SR switches between
Numerator Denominator
In such cases, Swap ratio =
Relevant factor of Acquiror firm
Relevant factor of Target firm
Tutorial Note: SR may be calc based on more than one factor EPS, MP & BVPS and then
weights are applied to calc final SR (Weighted Avg Swap Ratio)
Minimum Swap Ratio (Always from the point of view of Target)
Concept: 100% of Synergy gains shall accrue to the Acquiror. Hence, Required Post merger
EPS or MP should include full amount of synergy accruing to the Acquiror only
Based on Earnings
Min Swap -
Ratio
EPST
Revised EPS, (including whole
Synergy in earnings)
Based on Market Value
$MP_{T}$
Min Swap -
=
Ratio
Refer bottom of the page for Tabular format to calc Min SR
Tabular format to calc Max or Min SR
Revised $MP_{A}$ (including whole
Synergy in market value)
For Max SR: it is set equal to Pre-
merger EPS or MP of Acquiror
For Min SR: use revised $EPS_{A}$ or
$MP_{A}$ after incl 100% synergy gains.

*When to deduct & when NOT to deduct Cash & bank balance while calculating "Cost of Acq."?

stock & debtors

How to be decide Financial Feasibility of Acquisition?
General Points to Remember
If NPV is positive Acquisition is advantageous
If NPV is negative Acquisition is not advantageous
Students are under general impression that data in the 1st column belongs to Acquiror & in the 2nd
column belongs to the Target. But Q may prank you by writing Target Company data in 1st column &
Acquiror data in 2nd column.
Should $G/(L)$ to the sh hl be calculated in terms of MV or Earnings?
$G/(L)$ in terms of MV is always preferred over earnings. Hence if info about (i) PER or (ii) Synergy in MV
is available in Question then Calculate $G/(L)$ in terms of MV. Else Calc $G/(L)$ in terms of Earnings
If SR needs to be calculated & Q doesn't provide the basis to calculate SR, then use MP as the basis to
calculate SR. $[MP_{T}/MP_{A}]$
If Question doesn't provide as to what would be the post-merger PE Ratio then default assumption is
that "PE Ratio of Acquiror will remain maintained even after merger"
hence, $PER_{AT}=PER_{A}$ {aka Bootstrap effect}
If PER of Acq is 10 times & Tgt is 5 times and Q says "after merger PE ratio will be adversely affected
by 10%" then Post merger PE ratio will be taken as 9 times

10. If Question has written 'ignore synergy' next to Premerger PE ratio info eg. "PE ratio (ignore synergy)"
then there will be no synergy coming through PE ratio being same assumption. If no other kind of
synergy info is provided by Q then $V_{AT}=V_{A}+V_{T}.$
11. If Q language reads as "Considering MP of Target reflects its true value" then don't make the mistake
of applying PER of Acquiror to the earnings of Target. Instead, post merger market cap would be the
simple summation of Pre merger MV of acquiror + Pre merger MV of target. i.e. $V_{AT}=V_{A}+V_{T}$

14. In reverse calc, Turnover could be calc using either 'Inventory turnover ratio' or 'Debtors turnover
ratio'. However, if both are given in a Q then prefer 'Inventory turnover ratio' to calc turnover {Reason
→ Debtor turnover ratio will give only Credit sales. But Inventory turnover ratio will give COGS for
Total sales, now using GP ratio Total sales can be found}

(iv) In the above case, if Co. wishes that the ex-rights value of share shall not fall below 1900 (or 5% of

ratio?
Solve: Let R be the ratio in which right shares to be issued
$1900=\frac{2000\times1+1600\times R}{1+R}$
$\therefore R=1/3$ or 0.33:1
Hence, Co. will issue 1 right sh for every 3 sh held

Equity Buyback or share repurchase or Ownership Restructuring
Company buys its own equity share from the market thereby reducing the no. of equity shares Outstanding.
Buyback price is generally at a premium over current market price of share.
(i) Buyback price per share = Current MP + Buyback Premium per share
(ii) Total amount required for buyback = No. of Equity shares to be bought back x Buyback price per share

For BCD Ltd., before acquisition

Dividend
Price
+ Growth%
Cost of Capital i.e., $Ke=(0.60/20)+0.07=0.10$
After acquisition g (i.e. growth) becomes 0.08
Therefore, price per share after acquisition $=0.60/(0.10-0.08)=\overline{\times}30$
The increase in value therefore is = (30-20) × 5,00,000 = 50,00,000/-

Further PQR feels that management of XYZ Ltd. has been over paid. With better motivation, lower salaries and
fewer perks for the top management, will lead to savings of 4,00,000 p.a. Top management with their families
are promoters of XYZ Ltd. Present value of these savings would add 30,00,000 in value to the acquisition.
Following additional information is available regarding PQR Ltd.:
Required:
(i)
What is the maximum price per equity share which PQR Ltd. can offer to pay for XYZ Ltd.?
(ii)

their controlling interest?

40

$ER=0.875$

MERGERS, ACQUISITIONS & RESTRUCTURING
Study Material
The CEO of a company thinks that shareholders always look for EPS. Therefore he considers maximization of
EPS as his company's objective. His company's current Net Profits are 80 lakhs and $P/E$ multiple is 10.5. He
wants to buy another firm which has current income of 15.75 lakhs & $P/E$ multiple of 10.
What is the maximum exchange ratio which the CEO should offer so that he could keep EPS at the current
level, given that the current market price of both the acquirer and the target company are 42 and 105
respectively?
If the CEO borrows funds at 15% and buys out Target company by paying cash, how much should he offer to
maintain his EPS? Assume tax rate of 30%.
Solution
The correct way to write is 2.625:1
Thus, for every one share of Target Company 2.625 shares of Acquirer Company.
(ii) Let x lakhs be that amount paid by Acquirer company to Target Company. Then to maintain same EPS i.e.
4 the number of shares to be issued will be:
$=\frac{(80|akhs+15.75|akhs)-0.70\times15\%\times x}{20|akhs}=4$
$=\frac{95.75-0.105~x}{20}=4$
$X=\mathbb{X}150$ lakhs Thus, 150 lakhs shall be offered in cash to Target Company to maintain same EPS.

now felt that the company can be nursed back to health by proper financial restructuring and consequently
the following scheme of reconstruction has been devised:
(i)
Equity shares are to be reduced to 25/- per share, fully paid up;
(ii)
(iii)
(iv)
(v)
(vi)
Preference shares are to be reduced (with coupon rate of 10%) to equal number of shares of 50 each,
fully paid up
Debenture holders have agreed to forego interest accrued to them. Beside this, they have agreed to
accept new debentures carrying a coupon rate of 9%.
Trade creditors have agreed to forgo 25 per cent of their existing claim; for the balance sum they have
agreed to convert their claims into equity shares of 25/- each.
In order to make payment for bank loan and augment the working capital, the company issues 6 lakh
equity shares at $25/-$ each; the entire sum is required to be paid on application. The existing
shareholders have agreed to subscribe to the new issue.
While Land and Building is to be revalued at 250 lakh, Plant & Machinery is to be written down to 104
lakh. A provision amounting to 5 lakh is to be made for bad and doubtful debts.

sheet assuming the scheme of re-construction is implemented in letter and spirit.

PV of Cash Flows of Merged Entity after the forecast period

PV of $TV_{5}=\#7302.22~lakhs\times0.497=\#3629.20~lakhs$

1.
Shareholders of Leopard Ltd. will get one share in Tiger Ltd. for every two shares. External liabilities are
expected to be settled at 5,00,000. Shares of Tiger Ltd. would be issued at its current price of 15 per
share. Debenture holders will get 13% convertible debentures in the purchasing company for the same
amount. Debtors and inventories are expected to realize 2,00,000.
2.
Tiger Ltd. has decided to operate the business of Leopard Ltd. as a separate division. The division is likely
to give cash flows (after tax) to the extent of 5,00,000 per year for 6 years. Tiger Ltd. has planned that,
after 6 years, this division would be demerged and disposed of for 2,00,000.
3.
The company's cost of capital is 16%
Make a report to the Board of the company advising them about the financial feasibility of this acquisition.
Net present values for 16% for 1 are as follows:
Solution: (a) Calculation of Purchase Consideration
Net Present $Value=PV$ of Cash Inflow + PV of
Demerger of Leopard Ltd. - Cash Outflow
$=\mathbb{\times}5,00,000\times PVAF(16\%,6)+\mathbb{\times}2,00,000~PVF$
$(16\%,6)-:10,75,000$
$=\mathbb{7}5,00,000\times3.684+\mathbb{7}2,00,000\times0.410-$
10,75,000
= 18,42,000+82,000-10,75,000
= 8,49,000
Since NPV of the decision is positive it is
advantageous to acquire Leopard Ltd.

Rahul Ltd. has surplus cash of 100 lakhs and wants to distribute 27% of it to the shareholders. The company
decides to buy back shares. The Finance Manager of the company estimates that its share price after re-
purchase is likely to be 10% above the buyback price-if the buyback route is taken. The number of shares
outstanding at present is 10 lakhs and the current EPS is 3.
You are required to determine:
(i)
The price at which the shares can be re-purchased, if the market capitalization of the company should be
210 lakhs after buyback,
(ii)
The number of shares that can be re-purchased, and
(iii)
The impact of share re-purchase on the EPS, assuming that net income is the same.
Solution:
(i)
(ii)
(iii)
Let P be the buyback price decided by Rahul Ltd.
Market Capitalisation after Buyback
1.1P (Original Shares - Shares Bought Back)
$=1.1P(10~lakhs-\frac{27\%of~100~lakhs}{P})$
$=11~lakhs\times P-27~lakhs\times1.1=11~lakhsP-29.7~lakhs$
Again, 11 lakhs P - 29.7 lakhs
or 11 lakhs $P=210~lakhs+29.7~lakhs$
$r~P=\frac{239.7}{11}=\overline{7}21.79~Per~Share$
Number of Shares to be Bought Back :-
27 Lakhs 1.24 lakhs (approx.)
=
21.79
or 123910 share
New equity shares :-
10 lakhs-1.24 lakhs = 8.76 lakhs or
$0000-123910=876090~shares$
$\therefore EPS=\frac{3\times10~Lakhs}{8.79~Lakhs}=\overline{7}3.43$
Thus, EPS of Rahul Ltd, increases to 3.43

Basic Valuation Principle
If Q
Q is silent then prefer writing valuation
in both 'total' terms & 'per share' terms.
Value of any Asset today is the 'Present Value of Expected Cash Flows' from that Asset
discounted @ Required Rate of Return.
Here, Required rate of return is the Opportunity Cost of Capital in similar risky opportunities.

Earnings Capitalisation Model | Earnings Value of the Company
Future Maintainable Profits*
Value of business =
+ MV of Non-trade investments
Capitalization rate or Ke
*Future Maintainable profit
= Past year / last year profit
Remember to start with before tax profits
+
Add: Extraordinary loss in the past year
Less: Extraordinary gain eg. gain on sale of asset in the past year
Less: Addl Expenditure in future eg. addl advertisement exps
Add: Addl Income on expected geographical expansion/ addition of new product or new branch
etc [Sales - Variable costs - Fixed cost]
Less: Addl Depreciation on revaluation of assets
Less: Income from non- trade investments eg Intt on FD or Income from Inv in Mutual funds
= Future Maintainable Profit before tax
Less: Taxes
= FMP after taxes
Tutorial Note:
Remember to end with after tax profits
Earnings capitalization model assumes that Earnings will remain constant for infinite years.

UNDERVALUED. Hence an investor should buy shares of TCS.

How to calc growth rate
Eg.
Calc growth rates?
Solve: $G=RR\times ROE$ 6%
6%
10.8%
10.8%
10.8%
X Wrong answer
Correct Approach: $G_{current~year}=RR_{previous~year}\times ROE$
current year
i.e. $G_{1}=RR_{0}\times ROE_{1}$
Solve: $g_{n}=RR_{n-1}\times ROE_{n}$
3.
4.
!
Growth rate for 1st Year cannot be calculated beause we don't hv RR for $0^{th}yr$ However, if such
situation comes up in exam then assume $RR_{0}=RR_{1}$ & calc g₁
i.
Sometimes Students make the mistake of using "growth rate as discounting rate". Growth
rate is meant for growing earnings & dividends i.e. for compounding (not for discounting).
Since both K & g rates are given in % terms hence there is scope for confusion & mistake in
exams.
ii. $G=RR\times ROE$
Please use RR here. Student sometimes make the mistake of using DPR here
Whether given Dividend is $D_{0}$ or D₁?
eg. $DPR=60\%\&ROE=10\%$
Solve: $g=0.60\times10\%=6\%$ is wrong
If words "had/has paid/declared" are used or Dividend info is available from Income Statement then
given Dividend is assumed as $D_{0}$ In rest of the cases, ICAI assumes given Dividend as D₁ most of the times!
If Q gives both 'Coupon rate on bonds & Debentures' as well as 'effective interest rate' then use
effective interest rate to calc 'Interest Exps' on Income statement.

Earnings Growth Model
SECURITY VALUATION & BUSINESS VALUATION
It is just like Dividend growth model with only difference that "DPS" will be replaced by "EPS".
$P_{0}=\frac{E_{1}}{K_{e}-g}$
Walter's Model
$P_{c}=\frac{D+\frac{r}{k_{c}}(E-D)}{k_{c}}$
here,
Tutorial Note: In one of the Q of earnings
growth model ICAI has used ROE % as $K_{e}$
r means Rate of Return on retained earnings/
Return on equity/Return on investment
Why $\triangle P$ replaced by $=\frac{r}{k_{e}}(E-D)?$
Change in price takes place because of retained earnings.
If there is no retained earnings & co. distributes every
single it earns then share prices will not change. Hence
if we retain the earnings then share price increases. The
increase will be equal to PV of return on investment of
such retained earnings discounted at Ke [PVP]
Derivation of Walter's model
$P_{0}$ $=\frac{D_{1}+P_{1}}{1+K_{e}}=\frac{D+P_{1}}{1+K_{e}}$
$\Rightarrow1+K_{e}=\frac{D+P_{1}}{P_{o}}$
$\Rightarrow K_{e}=\frac{D+P_{1}}{P_{o}}-1.$
$\Rightarrow K_{e}=\frac{D+P_{1}-P_{o}}{P_{o}}$
$\Rightarrow K_{e}=\frac{D+\Delta P}{P_{o}}$
$\Rightarrow K_{c}=\frac{D+\frac{r}{K_{c}}(E-D)}{P_{o}}$
n
= 1 crore shares
$RR=40\%$
$ROE=20\%$
$Ke=15\%$
Calc Po using Walter's model
$\Rightarrow P_{c}=\frac{D+\frac{r}{K_{c}}(E-D)}{K_{c}}$
Solve :
$P_{c}=\frac{D+\frac{r}{k_{c}}(E-D)}{k_{c}}=\frac{18+\frac{0.20}{0.15}(30-18)}{0.15}$
Workings:
Earnings = 150 cr. x 20% = 30 cr
n
= 1 cr
$EPS=\mp30$
$=7226.67$
$DPS=\mp18$
EXAMPLE
Eq sh hl fund = 150 crores
Q. What if in above example DPR is decreased from 60% to 20% calc Po?
Solve:
$P_{o}=\frac{D+\frac{r}{ke}(E-D)}{ke}=\frac{6+\frac{0.20}{0.15}(30-6)}{0.15}=\overline{7}.253.33$
Q. Refer original example, suppose $Ke=25\%.$ Calc Po
Case (i) $DPR=60\%$
(ii) $DPR=20\%$
Solve:
$p_{o}=\frac{18+\frac{0.20}{0.25}(30-18)}{0.25}=\overline{7}110.4$
$p_{o}=\frac{6+\frac{0.20}{0.25}(30-6)}{0.25}=\overline{7}100.8$

Comment

Co. is exactly meeting sh hl expectations. Sh hl will be indifferent about
dividend policy.

- the actual DPR as well as optimum DPR, compare both $P_{0}$ and write your comment.
In exams, Gordon's model is preferred over Walter's model if Q is silent.
H Model
$g_{H}$
9L
High Growth Period
Time Low Growth Period
Explanation of the formula:
$\rho_{o}=\frac{D_{o}\times(1+g_{i})}{K_{e}-g_{i}}+\frac{D_{o}\times H\times(g_{H}-g_{i})}{K_{e}-g_{i}}$
here,
H means half life of higher growth period
The 1st component of the formula completely ignores the higher growth rate & simply assumes that only
lower growth rate will prevail for infinite years & accordingly calculates the PV of dividends growing at
lower growth rate.
The 2nd component of the formula takes into account the differential growth rate. However, since it is
a transition period & differential growth rate will gradually decline to 0% hence we multiplied it by H,
where h means half of the life of transition period.
Also, the incremental dividend during the transition period will exist not only during the transition
period, but it will also lift up the base for all the future dividends till perpetuity hence we used $k_{e}-g_{L}$ in
the denominator.
EXAMPLE
Solve:
Last Dividend = 15
Co. will grow @ 25% for 8 yrs (transition period) thereafter growth rate will fall to 10%
forever.
If $K_{e}=18\%$, Calc $P_{0}$ using H -Model
$P_{0}=\frac{D_{o}\times(1+g_{i})}{K_{e}-g_{i}}+\frac{D_{o}\times H\times(g_{\mu i}-g_{i})}{K_{e}-g_{i}}=\frac{15\times1.10}{0.18-0.10}+\frac{15\times4~yrs\times(0.25-0.10)}{0.18-0.10}=\overline{7}318.75.$
Exam Tip: Use "H model" in exams only when Q specifically says so, otherwise deal that situation with
Gordon's Model only.
It means if Q says "growth rate at present is 40% & will start falling in a liner manner so as to become
10% from 5th year onwards forever". In this case use Gordon's model only unless Q specifically asks
to use H Model in Exams

Why EBIT (1- )? or Why Tax benefit on interest is not considered while calc FCFF's ?
Since we disc. CFs by Ko which in itself incorporates after tax int. rates (i.e. tax benefit has been
considered in disc. rate itself ), there fore, again claiming tax benefit while calculating FCFF's would
amount to double counting of the same benefit.

Exam Tips
1.
Whether calc Depn on Opening WDV or on Op WDV + Capex?
If Q is silent then Depn must be calc on 'Op WDV + Capex' assuming capex is incurred during
the year (& not at the end of the yr)
2.
Which approach - FCFF or FCFE shall I use in exams?
If growth rate in free cash flows to the Firm is given then use FCFF approach.
If growth rate in free cash flows to the Equity is given then use FCFE approach.
If there in NO debt, then
$EAT=EBIT(1-t)$
$FCFE=FCFF$

ALCAR Model / Shareholder Value Analysis
Alcar model helps in determining the value of strategy.
Example: Co. wishes to launch a new product & plans to incur heavy expenditure on Research, Capex &
Advertisements, then how to find out whether strategy will be Value additive or not?
Value of strategy = Value of firm with strategy less Value of firm without strategy
Use FCF Approach as taught earlier to calc Value of firm with & without strategy
Decision: If value of strategy is positive then implement the strategy.
Exam Tip: Even if there is NO sales growth & hence no business expansion, still an amount of Capex
equivalent to Depn needs to be incurred to run the business & maintain the same level of sales.

PE Multiple Approach
SECURITY VALUATION & BUSINESS VALUATION
Relative Valuation Technique
Step 1: Find PER of a Comparable firm i.e. a Proxy firm
Step 2: Adjust PER to account for difference between Proxy firm & Firm to be valued.
Step 3: Apply Adjusted PER on EPS of Firm to be valued so as to find Fair MP.

PE Ratio $=30$ times

30 times 25 times
Same PER may or may not be applicable
Adjustments in PER are done to account for the differences in:
Goodwill/ Reputation
- Perceived Risk Level
- Less diversified vs Well diversified
PEG Multiple
PEG Multiple $=\frac{PE~Ratio}{g}$
Niche Technology, patents
Difference in growth rates etc.
PER of one Co. cannot be directly applied to another Co. PE Ratios differs due to difference in growth
rates hence we actually need to account for the diff. in growth rate as well.
PEG Multiple provides us PE ratio
per 1% of growth rate.
Note: Observe that prime facie, based on PE ratio, SBI appeared undervalued & Kotak appeared to be
most overvalued bank. However, based on PEG ratio, Kotak turned out to be the most undervalued bank.
EXAMPLE
If IDFC first bank has EPS of  2 & expected growth rate of 18%, calc relative val using
avg. PEG multiple of the banking sector
Avg PEG Multiple
$=\frac{3+3.33+2.5}{3}=2.94$
i.e. 2.94 is Avg PE multiple per 1% of growth
Applicable PE multiple for IDFC bank $=18\times2.94$
Fair price $=53~+imes\times\mp2EPS=\mp106$
$=52.98\sim53$ times

Asset side approach
Total Assets (excluding Non-trade inv, P&L $A/c$ Dr bal, Advance for purchase of Plant, Capital
WIP, L&B held as investment)
+ Items that encourage future earning power but not yet recorded as Assets in books eg.
Intangible Assets such as R&D, Advertising, Patent etc.
(-) Current Liabilities
(+) Non cash adjustment done in NOPAT [eg Provision for bad debts]

added back are not considered in the Weights

Enterprise value = MV of Equity

Cash & Cash Equivalents
1. Why Minority interest is added?
Since EV values a business in its entirety/ totality hence minority interest is also added. In other
words, it assumes that 100% of subsidiary cos. stake will also be bought while acquiring the target co.
Why 100% subsidiary stake? Since EV Multiples such as EV/Sales or EV/EBITDA uses
Consolidated Sales or Consolidated EBITDA that includes 100% subsidiary data in the them,
therefore, EV has to also include Value of minority interest for matching purposes.
2. Why Cash & cash Eq is deducted?
Cash is subtracted because it reduces the Net Cost of acquisition for a potential buyer

Cost - to
SECURITY VALUATION & BUSINESS VALUATION
Duplicate Approach
it values a startup by including all costs associated with the startup product development costs,
physical assets, customer acquisition cost.
Limitation of this Approach doesn't focus on future revenue projections or intangibles of the startup.
Comparable Transactions Method
The question being answered is "How much were similar startups valued at?"

discounted using this rate as follow:
The current price = 3.55 +46.19/(1.1395)=27.59

$EPS_{3}=\exists14.40(1+0.20)=\exists17.28$

$g_{7}=RR_{6}\times ROE_{7}$

remain the same]. The value of DESC's share 5 years from now will be
$=\frac{D_{6}}{k_{e}-g}=\frac{5.72}{15\%-12\%}=191$

(8 Marks) Exam May 2007
The following information is supplied to you:
₹
Ascertain whether the company is following an optimal dividend policy.
Find out what should be the $P/E$ ratio at which the dividend policy will have no effect on the value of the share.
Will your decision change, if the P/E ratio is 8 instead of 12.5?
CA, CFA (USA), CPA (USA) PRAVEEN KHATOD - Leaders in Advanced Financial Education Across India
64
Alpha Academy
Solution:
(i)
SECURITY VALUATION & BUSINESS VALUATION
The EPS of the firm is 10 (i.e., 2,00,000/20,000). The $P/E$ Ratio is given at 12.5 and the cost of capital,
k, may be taken at the inverse of $P/E$ ratio. Therefore, $k_{e}$ is 8% (i.e., 1/12.5). The firm is distributing total
dividends of 1,50,000 among 20,000 shares, giving a dividend per share of 7.50. the value of the
share as per Walter's model may be found as follows:
$P=\frac{D}{K_{e}}+\frac{(r/k_{e})(E-D)}{k_{e}}=\frac{7.50}{.08}+\frac{(.10/.08)(10-7.5)}{.08}=\overline{7}132.81$
The firm has a dividend payout of 75% (i.e., 1,50,000) out of total earnings of 2,00,000. Since, the rate
of return of the firm, r, is 10% and it is more than the $k_{e}$ of 8%, therefore, by distributing 75% of earnings,
the firm is not following an optimal dividend policy. The optimal dividend policy for the firm would be to
pay zero dividend and in such a situation, the market price would be
$P=\frac{D}{K_{e}}+\frac{(r/K_{e})(E-D)}{K_{e}}=\frac{0}{.08}+\frac{(.10/.08)(10-0)}{.08}=\overline{7}156.25$
So, theoretically the market price of the share can be increased by adopting a zero payout.
(ii) The $P/E$ ratio at which the dividend policy will have no effect on the value of the share is such at which the
$k_{e}$ would be equal to the rate of return, r, of the firm. The $K_{e}$ would be 10% $(=r)$ at the $P/E$ ratio of 10.
Therefore, at the $P/E$ ratio of 10, the dividend policy would have no effect on the value of the share.
(iii) If the $P/E$ is 8 instead of 12.5, then the $k_{e}$ which is the inverse of $P/E$ ratio, would be 12.5 and in such a
situation $k_{e}>r$ and the market price, as per Walter's model would be
$P=\frac{D}{K_{e}}+\frac{(r/K_{e})(E-D)}{K_{e}}=\frac{7.50}{.125}+\frac{(.1/.125)(10-7.5)}{.125}=\overline{7}76$
The optimal dividend policy for the firm would be to pay 100% dividend and market price of share in such
case would be
$P=\frac{10.0}{0.125}+\frac{(0.1/0.125)(10-10)}{0.125}=\overline{7}80$
Question 5
(8 Marks) Exam May 2012
X Ltd. has an internal rate of return @ 20%. It has declared dividend @ 18% on its equity shares, having face
value of 10 each. The payout ratio is 36% and Price Earnings Ratio is 7.25. Find the Cost of equity according to
Walter's Model and hence determine the limiting value of its shares in case the payout ratio is varied as per
the said model.
Solution: Internal Rate of Return (r) $=0.20$
Dividend (D)
$=1.80$
Earnings Per share $(E)=\frac{1.8\overline{0}}{0.36}=5$
Price of Share (P $)=5\times7.25=36.25$
$\Rightarrow p=\frac{D+\frac{r}{k_{s}}(E-D)}{k_{s}}\Rightarrow36.25=\frac{1.80+\frac{0.20}{k_{s}}(5-1.80)}{k_{s}}$
 $\Rightarrow36.25~k_{e}=1.80+\frac{0.20(3.20)}{k_{e}}\Rightarrow36.25~k_{e}=1.80+\frac{0.64}{k_{e}}$
$\Rightarrow36.25k_{e}^{2}=1.80k_{e}+0.64$
65
CA, CFA (USA), CPA (USA) PRAVEEN KHATOD - Leaders in Advanced Financial Education Across India
Alpha Academy
SECURITY VALUATION & BUSINESS VALUATION
$k_{e}=\frac{-b\pm\sqrt{b^{2}-4ac}}{2a}$
$k_{e}=\frac{-1.80\pm\sqrt{(1.80)^{2}-4(-36.25)\times0.64}}{2\times(-36.25)}$
$=\frac{-1.80\pm\sqrt{3.24+92.80}}{-72.50}=16\%$
Alternatively, it can also be calculated as follows:
$36.25~K_{e}{}^{2}-1.80~K_{e}-0.64=0$
Taking 36.25 common
$K_{e}{}^{2}-0.05~K_{e}-0.0176=0$
$K_{e}{}^{2}-0.16~K_{e}+0.11~K_{e}-0.0176=0$
$K_{e}(K_{e}-0.16)+0.11(K_{e}-0.16)=0$
$(K_{e}+0.11)(K_{e}-0.16)=0$
Since $K_{e}=-0.11$ is not possible, the possible answer shall be $K_{e}=0.16$ i.e. 16%.
Since the firm is a growing firm, then 100%
payout ratio will give limiting value of share
$=\frac{5.00+\frac{0.20}{0.16}(5-5)}{0.16}=\frac{5.00}{0.15}=\overline{7}.31.25$
Thus, limiting value is 31.25
Question 6
Alternatively, 0% payout ratio gives limiting
value of shares as follows:
$p=\frac{0+\frac{0.20}{0.16}(5-0)}{0.16}=\frac{1}{(0.16)^{2}}=\mathbb{\pi}39.06$
Thus, limiting value is 39.06

Following data is given to estimate the cost of equity capital:

You are required to calculate the Profit After Tax of ABC Ltd.
Additional Point:
Tutorial Note: If nothing else is mentioned then
Beta of ABC Ltd. means Equity beta of ABC Ltd.
Alternatively, if Q reads as "Asset beta of ABC
Ltd. $=0.90^{\prime\prime}$ then asset beta will be converted
into Equity beta using concept taught in
portfolio mngt chapter unit III.
$0.90=\beta_{e}\times\frac{170}{170+80(1-0.3)}+0$
 $\beta_{e}=1.1956$
& rest of the solution will change accordingly.
Solution: To compute Profit after Tax (PAT) of ABC Ltd. first we
shall compute Cost of Equity, Cost of Debt and WACC as follows:
Cost of Equity (k) as per CAPM
$k_{e}=8\%+0.90\times10\%=17\%$
Post Tax Cost of Debt
$(k_{d})=10\%(1-0.30)=7.00\%$
$WACC=17\%\times\frac{170}{250}+7\%\times\frac{80}{250}$
$=11.56\%+2.24\%=13.80\%$
EVA = Net Op Profit after Tax (NOPAT) - (Invested Capital x WACC)
$\vec{\times}31,10,000=NOPAT-(\vec{\times}2,50,000\times0.1380)$
$NOPAT=\overline{\times}65,60,000$
Operating Profit $=\frac{65,60,000}{0.70}=\overline{7}93,71,429$
Calculation of profit after Tax

Study Material (Similar), (8 Marks) Exam Nov 14 (Similar), May 18, RTP May 19
You are looking at the valuation of a Stable firm, Network Limited, done by an investment analyst. Based on an
expected free cash flows of 54 million for the following year and an expected growth rate of 9%, the analyst
has estimated the value of firm to be 1800 million. However, he committed a mistake of using the book value
of debt and equity. You do not know the book value weights employed by him but you know that the firm has a
cost of equity of 20% and post tax cost of debt of 10%. The market value of equity is thrice its book value,
whereas the market value of its debt is nine-tenth of its book value.
What is the correct value of the firm?
Solution: Cost of capital by applying Free Cash Flow to Firm (FCFF) Model is as follows:-
Value of Firm
$V_{0}=\frac{FCFF_{1}}{K_{c}-g_{n}}$
Thus, 1800 million = 54 million/(K-g)
Since $g=9\%$ then $Kc=12\%$
Now, let X be the weight of debt & given cost of equity $=20\%$ and cost of debt $=10\%$, then 20% $(1-X)+10\%X=12\%$
Hence, $X=0.80$ so book value weight for debt was 80%
Correct weight should be 60 of equity and 72 of debt.
Cost of capital = $=K_{c}=20\%(60/132)+10\%(72/132)=14.5455\%and$
Correct Value of Firm = 54 million/(0.1454-0.09) = 974.73 million.
CA, CFA (USA), CPA (USA) PRAVEEN KHATOD - Leaders in Advanced Financial Education Across India

Question 20
SECURITY VALUATION & BUSINESS VALUATION
Study Material, Exam Jan 2026, RTP May 2018, (8 Marks) MTP Oct 2022
SAM Ltd. has just paid a dividend of 2 per share and it is expected to grow @ 6% p.a. After paying dividend,
the Board declared to take up a project by retaining the next three annual dividends. it is expected that this
project is of same risk as the existing projects. The results of this project will start coming from the 4th year
onward from now. The dividends will then be 2.50 per share and will grow @ 7% p.a.
An investor has 1,000 shares in SAM Ltd. and wants a receipt of atleast 2,000 p.a. from this investment.
Show that the market value of the share is affected by the decision of the Board. Also show as to how the
investor can maintain his target receipt from the investment for first 3 years and improved income thereafter,
given that the cost of capital of the firm is 8%.
Solution: Value of share at present $:=\frac{D_{1}}{k_{e}-g}=\frac{2.(1.06)}{0.08-0.06}=\overline{7}106$
However, if the Board implement its decision, no dividend would be payable for 3 years and the dividend for
year 4 would be 2.50 and growing at 7% p.a. The price of the share, in this case, now would be:
$P_{o}=\frac{2.50}{0.08-0.07}\times\frac{1}{(1+0.08)^{3}}=\mathbb{7}198.46$
So, the price of the share is expected to increase from 106 to 198.45 after the announcement of the
project. The investor can take up this situation as follows:
In order to maintain his receipt at 2,000 for first 3 year, he would sell
At the end of 3rd year, he would be having 973 shares valued @ 250 each i.e. 2,43,250. On these 973
shares, his dividend income for year 4 would be @2.50i.e. 2,432.50.
So, if the project is taken up by the company, the investor would be able to maintain his receipt of at least
2,000 for first three years and would be getting increased income thereafter.

There is a privately held company X Pvt. Ltd that is operating into the retail space, and is now scouting for angel
investors. The details pertinent to valuing X Pvt. Ltd are as follows:
The company has achieved break even this year and has an EBITDA of 90. The leveraged overall beta based on
the industry in which it operates is 1.8, and the average debt to equity ratio is hovering at 40:60. The rate of
return provided by liquid bonds is 5%. The EV is to be taken at a multiple of 5 on EBITDA. The accountant has
informed that the EBITDA of 90 includes an extraordinary gain of 10 for the year, and a potential write off of
preliminary sales promotion costs of 20 are still pending. The internal assessment of rate of market return for
the industry is 11%.
The FCFs for the next 3 years are as follows:
The cost of debt (before tax assumed) will be 12%. Assume a tax regime of 30%. What is the potential value to
be placed on X Pvt. Ltd?
Solution
$1.8=$ Equity Beta x
Equity
or
Equity + Debt (1 - Tax)
$1.8=Equity~Beta\times\frac{.60}{.60+.40(1-0.30)}$
or Equity Beta $=2.64$ times
The adjusted EBITDA would be $90-10-20=60$
The EV will be multiple of 5 on the 60 obtained above $=300$
The Cost of equity in accordance with CAPM $\Lambda=5\%+2.64(11\%-5\%)=20.84\%$
The $NACC=Cost~of~Equity+Cost~of~Debt$
$=20.84(60/100)+12.0(1-0.3)(40/100)=15.864\%$

Finance
Startup financing means some initial infusion of money needed to turn an idea into reality.
Some of the Innovative Ways to Finance a Startup (4 Marks) May 19
Traditional lenders such as banks are not interested in startups.
LDR
30 Mins
LMR
O Mins
Here are some of the innovative sources for funding a startup:
Personal financing Important because investors will not put money into a deal if you have not
contributed any money from your personal sources.
(i)
(ii)
(iii)
(iv)
(v)
(vi)
(vii)
Personal credit lines Example - personal credit lines, Credit cards etc. However, banks grant personal
credit facility only when the business has enough cash flow to repay the line of credit.
Family and friends believe in you. However, loan obligations should always be in writing.
Peer-to-peer lending Business groups having similar faith or interest come together and generally
support each other.
Crowdfunding use of small amounts of capital from a large number of individuals through social
media and crowdfunding websites to bring investors and entrepreneurs together.
Microloans small loans issued by a single individual or aggregated across a number of individuals.
Vendor financing Vendor lends money to customers so that they can buy products from the company
itself. It includes extending the payment terms to a longer period or defer payment until the goods are
sold.
(viii) Purchase order financing In case of Startups inability to fund a large new order, Purchase order
financing companies often advance the required funds but directly to the supplier.
(ix) Factoring accounts receivables a facility is given to the seller to fund his receivables. Factor will pay
most of the sold receivables amount upfront and rest of the amount later.
Pitch Presentation
RTP Jan 2026
Pitch deck presentation is a brief presentation made either during face to face meetings or online meetings
using PowerPoint to investors explaining about the prospects of the company and why they should invest
How to approach a pitch presentation:
(i)
(ii)
(iii)
(iv)
(v)
Introduction give a brief account of yourself, milestones achieved etc. Use this opportunity to get
investors interested in your company.
Team Introduce the people behind the scenes who will make the product or service successful.
Investors are not only putting money towards the idea but they are also investing in the team. If
applicable, then highlight that the team has worked together in the past and achieved significant results.
Problem explain the problem you are going to solve. Investors should be convinced that the newly
introduced product or service will solve the problem.
Solution DESCRIBE how the company is planning to solve the problem. For instance, when Flipkart first
started e-commerce in India payment through credit card was rare. So they introduced cash on delivery.
Marketing/Sales Communicate the Market size of the product. This can include profiles of target
customers, how the promoter is planning to attract the customers.
(vi) Projections or Milestones It is difficult for a startup but an educated guess can be made. Projected
financial statements gives idea about where is the business heading? whether making profit or loss?

START UP FINANCE
Financial projections include three basic documents
•
Income statement: shows how much money business will generate.
• Cash flow statement: depict how much cash will be coming and how it will be utilized.
•
Balance sheet: shows overall finances including assets, liabilities and equity.
(vii) Competition highlight
- how the products or services are different from their competitors.
- If competitors have been acquired, give their complete details
(viii) Business Model is a wide term denoting core aspects of a business including purpose, business
process, target customers, offerings, strategies, infrastructure, organizational structures, sourcing,
trading practices, and operational processes and policies including culture.
A business model is the way in which a company generates revenue and makes a profit.
It is better to
show a list of the various revenue streams and a timeline for each of them,
how to price the product and what does the competitor charge
discuss the cost of customer acquisition, lifetime value of the customer and strategy to retain
customers.
(ix) Financing If already raised money, talk about
- how much money has been raised,
- who invested and
- what they did about it.
If pitching to raise capital, then list
- how much looking to raise and
- how intend to use the funds.
Unicorn
RTP Nov 2024, Sep 2025, MTP March 2024, Nov 2024, Jan 2026
A Unicorn is a privately held start-up company which has achieved a valuation of US\$ 1 billion. This term was
coined by venture capitalist Aileen Lee, first time in 2013. Unicorn, a mythical animal represents the
statistical rarity of successful ventures.
A start-up is referred as a Unicorn if it has following features:
(i)
A privately held start-up.
(ii)
Valuation of start-up reaches US\$ 1 Billion.
(iii)
Emphasis is on the rarity of success of such start-up.
(iv)
Other common features are new ideas, disruptive innovation, consumer focus, high on technology etc.
If the valuation slips below US\$ 1 billion it can lose its status of 'Unicorn'. Hence a start-up may be Unicorn at one
point of time and may not be at another point of time.
The next milestone is to become a Decacorn, i.e., attain a valuation of US\$ 10 billion.
In september 2011, InMobi, an ad-tech startup, became the first unicorn of India.
CA, CFA (USA), CPA (USA) PRAVEEN KHATOD - Best Faculty in India for Financial Management Courses
90
Alpha Academy
Modes of Financing for Startups
(i) Bootstrapping
START UP FINANCE
means build a company from personal finances or from the operating revenues of the new company.
It leads to cautious approach & curb wasteful expenditures towards marketing, offices and equipment.
Methods to bootstrap:
(a) Trade Credit prepare a well-crafted financial plan and pay a visit to the supplier's office.
Communication skills are important here.
The trick is to get the goods shipped, and sell them before one has to pay for them. It reduces the
working capital requirements.
(b) Factoring is a financing method where accounts receivable is sold to a commercial finance
company. The factor now assumes the task of collecting the receivables.
Merits -
- reduce costs associated with maintaining accounts receivable such as bookkeeping, collections
and credit verifications.
- frees up money tied up in receivables
(c) Leasing take the equipment on lease rather than purchasing it.
Benefits-
- reduce the capital cost
- claim tax exemption on lease rentals
- making smaller payments retain the ability to walk away from the equipment at the end of the
lease term.
(ii) Angel Investors
(4 Marks) MTP Oct 2019
Angel investors are affluent individuals who inject capital for startups in exchange for ownership
equity or convertible debt.
Salient Features of Angel Investors:
•
typically use their own money, unlike venture capitalists who take care of pooled money from
many other investors and place them in a strategically managed fund.
• usually represent individuals, but the entity that actually provides the fund may be a limited
liability company, a business, a trust or an investment fund, among many other kinds of vehicles.
• some angel investors invest through crowdfunding platforms online or build angel investor
networks to pool in capital.
• capital provided may be a one-time investment or an ongoing injection of money to support
through difficult early stages.
• provide more favorable terms compared to other lenders
• focused on helping startups rather than the possible profit they may get from the business.
• may lose their investments completely if startup fails.
(iii) Venture Capital Funds
Venture capital means funds made available for startup firms and small businesses with exceptional
growth potential.
Venture capital is money provided by professionals who alongside management invest in young,
rapidly growing companies that have the potential to develop into significant economic contributors.
CA, CFA (USA), CPA (USA) PRAVEEN KHATOD - Best Faculty in India for Financial Management Courses

*

START UP FINANCE

Venture Capital Funds could be in the form of (i) Trust, (ii) Company, or (iii) Limilited Liability Partnership.
Investors in Venture Capital Funds could be (i) Financial Institutions, (ii) Banks, (iii) Pension Funds, (iv)
Corporations, and (v) High Networth Individuals
Structure of Venture Capital Fund in India [MTP Sep 2025]
Three main types of fund structure exist: one for domestic funds and two for offshore ones:
(a) Domestic Funds Domestic Funds (i.e. one which raises funds domestically) are usually structured as:
(i) a domestic vehicle (either in the form of Trust or a Company) for the pooling of funds from the investor, and
(ii) a separate investment adviser that carries those duties of asset manager.
(b) Offshore Funds Two common alternatives available to offshore investors are: the "offshore structure" and
the "unified structure".
Offshore structure Under this structure, an investment vehicle (an LLC or an LP organized in a jurisdiction
outside India) makes investments directly into Indian portfolio companies.
Typically, the assets are managed by an offshore manager, while the investment advisor in India carries out
the due diligence and identifies deals.
Unified Structure When domestic investors are expected to participate in the fund, a unified structure is used.
Overseas investors pool their assets in an offshore vehicle that invests in a locally managed trust.
Domestic investors directly contribute to the trust.
Trust then makes the local portfolio investments.

Advantages of bringing VC in the company:
START UP FINANCE
It injects long-term equity finance which provides a solid capital base for future growth.
The venture capitalist is a business partner, sharing both the risks and rewards. Venture capitalists
are rewarded with business success and capital gain.
✓ Provide practical advice and assistance to the company based on past experience with other
companies which were in similar situations.

company. The venture capitalist may be capable of providing additional rounds of funding should
it be required to finance growth.

offering (IPO) of its shares onto the stock exchanges or overseas stock exchange such as NASDAQ.
✓ They can also facilitate a trade sale.

VC Investment Process
The entire VC Investment process can be segregated into the following steps:
1. Deal Origination VC gets deals directly or through intermediaries such as practicing Chartered Accountants.
VC indicates in advance about
✓ Sector focus
✓ Stages of business focus
Promoter focus
Turnover focus
Here the Company looking for VC funding provides Investment Memorandum which contains a detailed
business plan which consists of business model, financial plan, tentative valuation and exit plan.
2. Screening is generally carried out by a committee consisting of senior level people of the VC.
3. Due Diligence VC would now carry out due diligence in order to verify the veracity of the documents
taken. This is generally handled by external bodies, mainly renowned consultants. The fees of due
diligence could be paid by the VC or may be shared between the VC and the company.

4. Deal Structuring The deal is structured in such a way that both parties win. In many cases, the

Besides, VC may put a condition that promoter has also to sell part of its stake along with the VC. Such
a clause is called tag-along clause.

[Q. In Deal Structuring, in many structures to facilitate the exit, the Venture Capital may put a tag-

Post Investment Activity VC nominates its nominee in the board of the company to ensure that
Company adheres to certain guidelines like strong MIS, strong budgeting system, strong corporate
governance, professional management and achievement of milestones. If milestone has not been
met the company has to give explanation to the VC.
Exit plan Mainly, exit happens in two ways:
(i)
'Sell to third party(ies)': This sale can be in the form of IPO or Private Placement to other VCs.
(ii) Promoter would give a buy back commitment at a pre agreed rate (generally between IRR of 18%
to 25%). In many deals, the promoter buyback is the first refusal method adopted i.e. the
promoter would get the first right of buyback.
Startup India Initiative
or Q. NIYA Healthcare is a proprietary concern engaged in the manufacture and development of
Pharmaceutical products since last five years. To scale up the business operations and increase the present
turnover which is hovering around 500 Million, the proprietor decides to convert his existing business into a
Private Limited Company. He also wants to get access to various tax benefits, easier compliances under the
startup India initiative and get recognized as a startup company.
Advise whether NIYA Healthcare can be recognized as a startup company in view Of the criteria considered
eligible for the startup recognition initiated by the Government of India? (4 M) Exam N19, N23, RTP N23
Startup India scheme was initiated by the Government of India on 16th of January, 2016.
An entity shall be considered as a Startup:
* Upto a period of 10 years from the date of incorporation/registration. It could be incorporated as either
a Private Limited Company or a Registered Partnership Firm or a Limited Liability Partnership in India.
Turnover for any of the financial years has not exceeded 100 crores, and
*
Working towards innovation, development or improvement of products or processes or services, or if
it is a scalable business model with a high potential of employment generation or wealth creation.
Provided that an entity formed by splitting up or reconstruction of an existing business shall not be
considered a 'Startup'.

Succession Planning in Business
RTP May 2024, (4 Marks) Exam Nov 2024
Succession planning is the process of identifying the critical positions within an organization and developing
action plans for individuals to assume those positions. A succession plan identifies future need of people
with the skills and potential to perform leadership roles. Succession planning is an important priority for
family owned businesses as most of them are managed by a non-family leader even though the ownership
lies with the family. Taking a holistic view of current and future goals, this type of preparation ensures that
the right people are available for the right jobs today and in the years to come. It can also provide a liquidity
event, which enables the transfer of ownership in a going concern to rising employees. Succession planning
is a good way for companies to ensure that businesses are fully prepared to promote and advance all
employees-not just those who are at the management or executive levels.
Why is there a need for succession planning?
MTP April 2024
Risk mitigation If existing leader quits, then searches can take six-nine months for suitable candidate to
close. Keeping an organization without leader can invite disruption, uncertainty, conflict and endangers
future competitiveness.
Cause removal If the existing leader is culpable of gross negligence, fraud, willful misconduct, or
material breach while discharging duties and has been barred from undertaking further activities by
court, arbitral tribunal, management, stakeholders or any other agency.
Talent pipeline Succession planning keep employees motivated and determined as it can help them
obtaining more visibility around career paths expected, which would help in retaining the knowledge
bank created by company over a period of time and leverage upon the same.
Conflict Resolution Mechanism This planning is very helpful in promoting open and transparent
communication and settlement of conflicts.
Aligning In family owned business succession planning helps to align with the culture, vision, direction
and values of the business.
CA, CFA (USA), CPA (USA) PRAVEEN KHATOD - Best Faculty in India for Financial Management Courses

competencies required to perform the role successfully.

whether there is a need to search outside the organization.

develop the business and prepare young family members for leadership role.

(1)
(2)
(3)

different from the way that a traditional corporate manager thinks, and this puts off seasoned
corporate leaders from joining even matured start-ups.
Premature for startups to implement business succession Certain startups are at early growth stage
and too much of processes would lead to growth slow-down.
Founders are the face of startups One cannot imagine a startup without a founder who initiated the
idea and executed it and in his/her absence succession planning can become difficult.

Risk of an Individual Security
Deviation from Expected outcome is Risk.
PORTFOLIO MANAGEMENT
Lesser the deviations, Lesser would be the risk
Higher the deviations, Higher would be the risk
If we can measure the extent of deviation, we have actually measured the Risk.
To measure deviation, we use a statistical concept called as "Standard Deviation".

Stock Selection - Based on Risk & Return considerations
1.
If two stocks have same Risk ---> Prefer stock having Higher Return
2.
If two have same return ---> Prefer stock having Lower Risk.
3.
If one of the stock has both Higher Return as well as lower risk ---> Prefer that stock.
4.
If one of the stock has higher return but also has higher risk ---> See example below.
CA, CFA (USA), CPA (USA) PRAVEEN KHATOD - Leaders in Advanced Financial Education Across India
99
Alpha Academy
PORTFOLIO MANAGEMENT
An Aggresive Investor (risk lover/risk seeker) would prefer investing in Vi since it has higher
returns%.
A Defensive investor (risk averse) would prefer investing in Airtel since it carries lower risk.
However, a rational investor would base his decision on 'Coefficient of Variation' as calc below. A
Risk neutral investor would prefer investing in Airtel since it has lower CV.
Coefficient of variation
$\frac{0}{\overline{x}}$ $=\frac{Risk}{Return}$ or
$CV_{vi}=\frac{18\%}{25\%\%}=0.72$ $CV_{Airtei}=\frac{10\%}{15\%}=0.667$
Return on Portfolio [R, or  ]
CV tells us risk being taken to earn every
1% of return. Lower CV is preferred
Return on Portfolio is weighted Average Return on individual securities where beginning of the
period Market values are the assigned weights.
!
$R_{p}=\Sigma R_{i}\times W_{i}$
EXAMPLE
Airtel declared dividend of 2 per share & ended the year with price of 350. TCS declared a
generous dividend of 50 per share & trades@2200 at the end of the year. Calc Return on Portfolio?
Return on
$lirte|=\frac{D_{1}+P_{1}-P_{0}}{P_{0}}\times100=\frac{2+350-300}{300}\times100=17.33\%.$
Return on $TCS=\frac{50+2200-2000}{2000}\times100=12.5\%$
1. Don't make the mistake of using No. of shares or Market Price as Weights. The correct
Weights are 'Market Values'.
2. Don't make the mistake of using Year-end Market Values as Weights. The correct Weights
while calc returns are Beginning of the period Market Values.
Exam Tip:
Weights should be takes either accurate (Numerator denominator format) or upto 4 decimal places

Risk of Portfolio $[\sigma_{p}]$
as per Modern Portfolio Theory/ Modern Approach or Harry
Markowitz Model or Risk-Return Optimization Approach
Risk of Portfolio is weighted avg risk of individual securities
Risk of Portfolio is NOT the weighted average risk of individual securities. Instead $\sigma_{p}$ is Less than
weighted average. This is so because multiple securities in the portfolio tend to offset each others
deviation & hence the net effect of deviation at portfolio-level will be less than the W.A.
Airtel
Portfolio
→TCS
$\sigma_{p}=\sqrt{(\sigma_{A}w_{A})^{2}+(\sigma_{B}w_{B})^{2}+2~\sigma_{A}w_{A}\sigma_{B}w_{B}Corr_{AB}}$

Q. Calc Risk of Portfolio if weight of Airtel is 0.30?
$Correlation_{As}=\frac{Covariance_{As}}{\sigma_{A}\sigma_{s}}=\frac{19.31}{17.05\times8.84}=0.128.$
$\sigma_{p}=\sqrt{(\sigma_{A}w_{A})^{2}+(\sigma_{B}w_{B})^{2}+2~\sigma_{A}w_{A}\sigma_{B}w_{B}Corr_{AB}}$
$=\sqrt{(17.05\times0.30)^{2}+(8.84\times0.70)^{2}+2\times17.05\times0.30\times8.84\times0.70\times0.128}$
$=8.52\%$
Verification that risk of portfolio is LESS than W.A.
$=17.05\%\times0.30\times+8.84\%\times0.70$
Interpretation of Covariance & Correlation
Covariance
1.
✓
$=11.30\%$
Denotes co-movement of two securities i.e. how the two securities will move together.
If Covariance is +ve then the two securities will usually move in the same direction.
If Cov is -ve then the two sec usually tend to move in the opposite direction.
If Cov is +ve the Corr will also be +ve & vice-versa.

Infact, $\sigma_{p}=W.A.$ Subtraction of
risk of Individual securities.
$\sigma_{p}=\sigma_{A}\times w_{A}-\sigma_{B}\times w_{B}$
or vice versa.
If in a particular year security
A delivers 20% return (which
is 10% above the mean or 20
above the mean) then Corr = +
1 implies that sec B will deliver
also return which are 20 above
its mean return
..Return on sec B
$=16\%+2\times9\%$
Risk of Portfolio will be highest
when corr = +1 since there will be
no offsetting effect.
In fact, $\sigma_{p}=W.A$ summation of
risk of Individual securities.

EXAMPLE
←
Suppose an investor has 10 lakhs of his personal funds, how can he construct an efficient
portfolio giving expected returns of 20% & what will be the risk of this portfolio. Given $R_{f}=8\%$, $\&R_{m}=15\%$ & $\sigma_{m}=5\%$
Solve:

$20\%=8\%\times(1-x)+15\%\times(1-x)+15\%\times X$
$0.20=0.08-0.08x+0.15x$
$x=1.7143$
Thus, borrow 71.43% of own funds @Rf i.e. 714300.
Now, invest total 1714300 in the market.
...Risk of above portfolio $=5\%\times1.7143=8.57\%$

Alpha Academy
Concept of Dominance
PORTFOLIO MANAGEMENT
To dominate other securities in the portfolio, a security must have any one of the below properties:
For the same level of risk, it has higher returns
For the same level of Returns, it has lower risk
A Security has both Higher Return & Lower Risk
Which securities dominate the other securities in the portfolio?
Solve:
Between A & B Sec A Dominates Sec B since for the same level of risk, it offers higher return $[A>B]$
Note: '>' is the Symbol of Dominance
Between A & C Sec C dominates Sec A Since for the same level of return it has lower risk $[C>A]$
Between D & E Sec D dominates sec E since it has both higher returns as well as lower risk $[D>E]$
Answer: Sec C, D & F dominates the other securities in the portfolio.
Exam Tip: How do I know whether to apply 'Concept of Dominance' or 'Coefficient of
Variation' in a particular Q in exam?
Hint: If Q asks for selecting more than one securities then apply 'Concept of Dominance'
If Qasks for selecting just one security then use 'Coefficient of Variation'.

Exam Tip: Beta value in answer must be written upto 3 decimal places.
Investment Decisions Using B
If market is expected to be bullish, prefer investing in high beta stock $(\beta>1).$ Such stocks are also called as
aggressive stocks.
If market is expected to be bearish, prefer investing in Low beta stock $(\beta<1).$ Such stocks are also called as
Defensive stocks.

r means correlation
$r^{2}$ means coefficient of determination
here, $r^{2}$ means what proportion of Total

market related factors

Unsystematic Variance (ε²)
[Balancing figure]
$\sigma_{i}^{2}-(\beta_{i}\sigma_{m})^{2}$
Total To Var - Sys Var
$\sigma_{i}^{2}(1-{r_{im}}^{2})$ $\sigma_{i}^{2}-(\sigma_{i}^{2}\times r_{im}^{2})$
!
Caution Note
Remember that it is $1-r^{2}$
NOT (1 - r)²
1 - r² means remaining proportion of Total
variance that is unexplained by the
market & hence attributed to
Unsystematic factors
i.e. $1-r^{2}=\frac{Unsystematic~Variance}{Tota|~Variance}$
If coefficient of determination i.e. $r^{2}=0.25(say)$ is given in Q & Correlation needs to be found then
$r=\sqrt{r^{2}}=\sqrt{0.25}=0.50$

$\epsilon_{p}^{2}=\Sigma(\epsilon_{i}\times w_{i})^{2}$
as per

as per
] Sharpe model
Derivation: You may recall that
$\sigma_{p}^{2}=(\sigma_{A}w_{A})^{2}+(\sigma_{B}w_{B})^{2}+2~\sigma_{A}w_{A}\sigma_{B}w_{b}Corr_{A}$ AB
On the same lines
$:\epsilon_{p}^{2}=(\epsilon_{A}w_{A})^{2}+(\epsilon_{B}w_{B})^{2}+2~\epsilon_{A}w_{A}\epsilon_{B}w_{B}Corr_{AB}$
here,
$Corr_{AB}=0$
Hence formula reduces down to
$\epsilon_{p}^{2}=(\epsilon_{A}w_{A})^{2}+(\epsilon_{B}w_{\beta})^{2}$
or
$\epsilon_{p}^{2}=\Sigma(\epsilon_{p}\times w_{i})^{2}$

Covariance $b/w$ 2 Securities can be calc as:
$Co~v_{ij}=\beta_{i}\beta_{j}\sigma_{m}^{2}.$
Derivation
$r_{ij}=r_{im}\times r_{jm}$
multiply both the sides by σ₁ $\sigma_{j}$
$r_{ij}\times\sigma_{i}\times\sigma_{j}=r_{im}\times\sigma_{i}\times r_{jm}\times\sigma_{j}$
multiply & Divide RHS by $\sigma_{m}^{2}$
$r_{ij}\times\sigma_{i}\times\sigma_{j}=r_{im}\times\frac{\sigma_{i}}{\sigma_{m}j}\times r_{im}\times\frac{\sigma_{j}}{\sigma_{m}j~L_{m}j}^{2}$
$cov_{ij}=\boxed{\beta_{i}}\times\beta_{j}\times\sigma_{m}^{2}}$

How much Return can we actually

& analysis on that particular stock by

Factor Model | Arbitrage Pricing Theory Model [APTM]
is an expanded version of CAPM i.e. $E(r)$ or $R_{j}=R_{f}+\beta(R_{m}-R_{f})$
Let's break down $\beta\&R_{m}-R_{f}$ into various factors it comprises of:
$E(r)OMR_{j}=R_{4}+\beta_{Forex}(R_{m\cdot Forex}-R_{t})+\beta_{Int+Rotes}(R_{m\cdot Inttes}-R_{f})+\beta_{Intion~Rotes}$ (Rm - Infl. Rate - Rf) +
$MRP_{Forex}$
Symbolically,
$MRP_{Intt~rates}$
$MRP_{Infl.Rate}$
E (r) or $Rj=\lambda_{0}+\beta_{i1}1~\Lambda_{1}+\beta_{i2}\Lambda_{2}+......................\beta_{in}\Lambda_{n}$
here,
$\lambda_{0}$ means Risk-free rate
$\lambda_{1}$ to $\lambda_{n}$ means Market Risk Premium for taking factor 1 to n risk
$\beta_{i1}$ to $\beta_{in}$ means Beta on an individual sec w.r.t factor 1 to nth factor risk
CA, CFA (USA), CPA (USA) PRAVEEN KHATOD - Leaders in Advanced Financial Education Across India
122
Alpha Academy
PORTFOLIO MANAGEMENT
APTM or Factor Model Vs. Multi factor Macro economic Model
APTM
$E(r)_{i}=R_{f}+\beta_{i1}\times MRP_{1}+\beta_{i2}\times MRP_{2}+.....\beta_{in}\times MRP_{n}$
Multi factor Macro-economic Model
$R_{i}=E(r)_{i}+\beta_{i1}(Diff.in~factor_{1})+\beta_{i2}(Diff.in~factor_{2})...$
Actual value minus Expected
value of Macroeconomic variable
Merged version by ICAI
G
R₁or $E(r)_{i}=R_{f}+\beta_{i1}$ (Diff. in factor₁) $+\beta_{i2}$ (Diff. in factor2)....
or $R_{f}+\beta_{i1}$(Actual value - Expected Value) $+\beta_{i2}$ (Actual Value - Expected Value) + ........
Portfolio Management Strategies / Portfolio Rebalancing Strategies
Passive Portfolio Strategy
Buy & Hold Strategy
The money you can't afford to loose
Active Portfolio Strategy
Formula Plans
Constant Amount Plan
Constant Proportion
Constant Ratio Plan
Portfolio Insurance
(ie money equal to floor value) is kept in Rf.
Variable Ratio Plan
Policy [CPPI]
Invest the money you can afford to loose
(ie money in excess of floor value) in stocks.
Constant Amount Plan [aka Constant Value Plan or Constant Dollar/Rupee Value Plan]
First, Decide a Constant Amount with which we shall remain invested in Equity at all the times,
Eg. Total Amount available = 15 lakhs and out of which say 7.5 lakhs will always be kept in Equity.
Keep the remaining amount of  7.5 lakhs in Debt or Rf or Cash.
1. Action to rebalance?
If stock price goes down and hence the Value
of Equity portfolio also goes down, then take
out money from Rf Asset and Invest in Equity.
2.
If stock price goes up and hence the Value of
Equity portfolio also goes up, then take out
money from Equity and Invest in Rf Asset.
How much amount of stock to buy/ sell at the time of Rebalancing the portfolio ?
An amount that brings back the Value of Equity to the originally decided Constant
Amount (say, 7.5 lakhs in our case)
3. When to Rebalance the portfolio?
An Investor has to set a Trigger for himself, say, whenever Value of Equity falls/ rises by
10% of the Originally decided Constant Equity Amount. Hence, trigger will be 75000 in our
case. Any fall/rise by 75000 or more will trigger rebalancing action.
CA, CFA (USA), CPA (USA) PRAVEEN KHATOD - Leaders in Advanced Financial Education Across India
123
Alpha Academy
Constant Ratio Plan
PORTFOLIO MANAGEMENT
Same as constant amount plan but instead of setting a constant amount, we decide a Constant Ratio, say
1:1 to be maintained between Equity & Debt/Rf/Cash. Now as Equity Value goes Up/Down, an Investor
will trigger the rebalancing action whenever Ratio deviates by a predetermined value, say by 10%.
Hence either 0.90:1 or 1.1:1 will trigger rebalancing action in the present case in order to bring the ratio
back to 1:1
Variable Ratio Plan
Same as constant ratio plan but Ratio of allocation between Equity & Debt/Rf/Cash is changed
depending upon the Stock Price levels. i.e. increasing the allocation % to Equity when Stock prices are
going down and vice-versa. Such Variable Ratio will always be given in Qitself.
Format for presentation of above Portfolio Rebalancing Strategies
Constant Proportion Portfolio Insurance / Investment Policy [CPPI]
If an investor has, say, 5 lakhs & he wants to ensure that his total value of investment shall not fall
below, say, 4.75 lakhs, ( 4.75 lakhs is termed as 'Floor value', resulting in a cushion of 25000) in
such situations we apply CPPI method.
What
happens
in CPPI
EXAMPLE
When Cushion (Safety Margin) increases then Allocation to Equity increases & vice-versa.
✓ Cushion = 'Current Portfolio value' less Floor Value
'Floor Value' means The Minimum value that an investor would like to insure at all the
time. It is something that an investor has to decide for himself.
✓ Multiplier =
1
Max crash % on any single day
✓ Amount To be Kept in equity = Multiplier x Cushion value
You have 500000 for investment
Floor Value =  475000
Max Crash $\%=12.5\%$
Decide Initial Inv. in Eq. & Debt as per CPPI.

☑ How to identify whether a Portfolio is Well diversified or Poorly
diversified?
A Portfolio having higher value of $1-r^{2}$ is considered as poorly
diversified portfolio because
form part of the deviation.
$1-r^{2}$ explains the proportion of Total Variance that comes from
carrying Unsystematic risk.

A well diversified portfolio has lower Unsystematic Risk i.e. lower $1-r^{2}$
Sortino Ratio better is the
performance

Question 1
PORTFOLIO MANAGEMENT
Study Material (Similar)
A stock costing \$100 pays no dividends. The possible prices that the stock might sell for at year-end and the
probability of each are:
a. What is the expected return on the stock?
b. What is the standard deviation of the expected return?
Solution:
$\sigma=\sqrt{Variance}$
$=\sqrt{55.25}$
!
$=7.43\%$
Caution Note While calculating Return%, Don't make the mistake of comparing
\$95 with \$90 & then Comparing \$100 with \$95. The prices given in the Table are
Year-end prices & all these prices should be compared with Initial Price of \$100.
Question 2
Study Material, RTP May 2023
Following information is available in respect of dividend, market price and market condition after one year.
The existing market price of an equity share is 106 (F.V. Re. 1), which is cum 10% bonus debenture of 6 each,
per share. $M/s$ X Finance Company Ltd. had offered the buy-back of debentures at face value.
Find out the expected return and variability of returns of the equity shares.
And also advise-Whether to accept buy back offer?
CA, CFA (USA), CPA (USA) PRAVEEN KHATOD - Leaders in Advanced Financial Education Across India
129
Alpha Academy
PORTFOLIO MANAGEMENT
Solution: The Expected Return of the equity share may be found as follows:
Expected Return $=(24\times0.25)+(12\times0.50)+(0\times0.25)=12\%$
The variability of return can be calculated in terms of standard deviation.
Var
$=0.25(24-12)^{2}+0.50(12-12)^{2}+0.25(0-12)^{2}$
$=0.25(12)^{2}+0.50(0)^{2}+0.25(-12)^{2}$
$=36+0+36$
SD
$=\sqrt{72}$
SD
$=8.485~o$ say 8.49
(*) The present market price of the share is 106 cum bonus 10% debenture of 6 each; hence the net cost is
100 (There is no cash loss or any waiting for refund of debenture amount).
M/s X Finance company has offered the buy back of debenture at face value. There is reasonable 10% rate of
interest Compared to expected return 12% from the market. Considering the dividend rate and market Price
the creditworthiness of the company seems to be very good. The decision regarding buy-back Should be taken
Considering the maturity period and opportunity in the market. Normally, if the maturity period is low say up
to 1 year better to wait otherwise to opt buy back option.

CA, CFA (USA), CPA (USA) PRAVEEN KHATOD - Leaders in Advanced Financial Education Across India

Alpha Academy
Solution:
(i)
PORTFOLIO MANAGEMENT
Investment committed to each security would be:-
(ii) The equation of critical line takes the following form:-
$W_{B}=a+bW_{A}$
Substituting the values of $W_{A}$ & $W_{B}$ from portfolio X and Y in above equation, we get
$0.40=a+0.30b$ and
$0.50=a+0.20b$
Solving above equation we obtain the slope and intercept, $a=070$ and $b=-1$ and thus, the critical line is
$W_{B}=0.70-W_{A}$
If half of the funds is invested in security A then,
$W_{B}=0.70-0.50=0.20$
Since $W_{A}+W_{B}+W_{C}$
$=1$
$W_{c}=1-0.50-0.20=0.30$
Tutorial Note: If weight of one of the
security comes out to $be>1$ then
some other security will have
negative weights meaning short sales.
Question 6
Study Material, RTP Nov 2022, MTP Oct 2022
A Ltd has an expected return of 22% and Standard deviation of 40%. B Ltd. has an expected return of 24% and
Standard deviation of 38%. A Ltd. has a beta of 0.86 and B Ltd. a beta of 1.24. The correlation coefficient
between the return of A Ltd. and B Ltd. is 0.72. The Standard deviation of the market return is 20%. Suggest:
(i)
Is investing in B Ltd. better than investing in A Ltd.?
(ii)
If you invest 30% in B Ltd. and 70% in A Ltd., what is your expected rate of return and portfolio Standard
deviation?
(iii)
What is the market portfolios expected rate of return and how much is the risk-free rate?
(iv)
What is the beta of Portfolio if A Ltd's weight is 70% and B Ltd's weight is 30%?
Solution:
(i)
A Ltd. has lower returns and higher risk. Therefore, investing in B Ltd. is better than in A Ltd because B ltd.
has both higher returns and lower risk. However, investing in both will yield diversification advantage.
(ii)
$r_{AB}=.22\times0.7+.24\times0.3=22.6\%$
$\sigma_{AB}^{2}=0.40^{2}\times0.7^{2}+0.38^{2}\times0.3^{2}+2\times0.7\times0.3\times0.72\times0.40\times0.38=0.1374$
$\sigma_{AB}=\sqrt{\sigma_{AB}^{2}}=\sqrt{.1374}=.37=37\%^{*}$
*Answer $=37.06\%$ is also correct and variation may occur due to approximation.

Question 7
Study Material, Exam May 2012
A has portfolio having following features:
You are required to find out the risk of the portfolio if the standard deviation of the market index ( $(\sigma_{m})$ is 18%.
Solution:
As per ICAI Suggested Answer, two alternative solutions are possible, below is one of those alternative
solution that we believe is more logical
$\beta_{p}:=\sum_{i=1}^{4}X_{i}\beta_{i}$
= $1.60\times0.25+1.15\times0.30+1.40\times0.25+1.00\times0.20$
$=0.4+0.345+0.35+0.20=1.295$
Systematic variance of portfolio $={\beta_{p}}^{2}\times{\sigma_{m}}^{2}=(1.295)}^{2}(18)^{2}=543.36$
Unsystematic variance of portfolio = $\div\sum_{i=1}^{4}(\sigma_{ei}^{2}\times w_{i}^{2})=(0.25)^{2}(7)^{2}+(0.30)^{2}(11)^{2}+(0.25)^{2}(3)^{2}+(0.20)^{2}(9)^{2}(9)^{2})$
$=3.0625+10.89+0.5625+3.24$
$=17.755$
Total variance = Systematic variance + Unsystematic variance $=543.36+17.755=561.115$
The Standard Deviation (Risk) of the portfolio $=[561.115]^{1/2}=23.69\%$

Question 8
Study Material, RTP Nov 2020
A study by a Mutual fund has revealed the following data in respect of three securities:
The standard deviation of market portfolio (BSE Sensex) is observed to be 15%.
(i)
What is the sensitivity of returns of each stock with respect to the market?
(ii)
What are the covariances among the various stocks?
(iii)
What would be the risk of portfolio consisting of all the three stocks equally?
(iv)
What is the beta of the portfolio consisting of equal investment in each stock?
(v)
What is the total, systematic and unsystematic risk of the portfolio in (iv)?
Solution:
(i) Sensitivity of each stock with market is given by its beta.
Standard deviation of market Index $=15\%$
Variance of market Index $=0.0225$
Beta of stocks $=r\times\sigma_{i}/\sigma_{m}OR~\sigma_{i}\times r/\sigma_{m}$
$A=20\times0.60/15=0.80$
$B=18\times0.95/15=1.14$
$C=12\times0.75/15=0.60$
(ii) Covariance between any 2 stock $=\beta_{1}\beta_{2}{\sigma^{2}}_{m}^{2}$
$Cov_{AB}=0.80\times1.14\times15^{2}=205.20$
(iii)
Covariance matrix
$Cov_{AC}=0.80\times0.60\times15^{2}=108$
$Cov_{Bc}=1.14\times0.60\times15^{2}=153.90$
Total risk of the equally weighted portfolio (Variance) $=400(1/3)^{2}+324(1/3)^{2}+144(1/3)^{2}+2(205.20)$
$(1/3)^{2}+2(108.0)(1/3)^{2}+2(153.900)(1/3)^{2}=200.244$
(iv)
ẞ of equally weighted portfolio =
$\beta_{p}=\Sigma\beta_{i}/N=\frac{0.80+1.14+0.60}{3}=0.8467$
(v)
Systematic Risk βρ² $m^{2}=(0.8467)^{2}(15)^{2}=161.302$
Unsystematic Risk
= Total Risk - Systematic Risk
$=200.244-161.302$
$=38.942$

Question 9
Study Material, (8 Marks) Exam May 19 (Similar), RTP May 18, MTP Nov 24, May 25
Following are the details of a portfolio consisting of three shares:
Standard Deviation of Market Portfolio Returns $=10\%$
You are given the following additional data:
Covariance (A,B) $=0.030$
Covariance $(A,C)=0.020$
Covariance $(B,C)=0.040$
Calculate the following:
(i)
The Portfolio Beta
(ii)
Residual Variance of each of the three shares
(iii)
Portfolio Variance using Sharpe Index Model [Alt language: Portfolio variance considering co-movemnt
between securities due to change in the market index]
(iv)
Portfolio Variance (on the basis of modern portfolio theory given by Markowitz) [Alt language: Portfolio
variance considering correlation between each pair of securities]
Solution:
(i)
(ii)
Portfolio Beta
$0.20\times0.40+0.50\times0.50+0.30\times1.10=0.66$
Residual Variance
To determine Residual Variance first of all we shall compute the Systematic Risk as follows:
${\beta_{A}}^{2}\times{\sigma_{M}}^{2}=(0.40)^{2}(0.10)^{2}=0.0016$
$\hat{\beta_{B}}^{2}\times\sigma_{M}}^{2}=(0.50)^{2}(0.10)^{2}=0.0025$
${\beta_{c}}^{2}\times{\sigma_{M}}^{2}=(1.10)^{2}(0.10)^{2}=0.0121$
Residual variance
A $0.015-0.0016=0.0134$
B $0.025-0.0025=0.0225$
C
$.100-0.0121=0.0879$
(iii) Portfolio Variance using Sharpe Index Model
Systematic Variance of Portfolio $=(0.10)^{2}\times(0.66)^{2}=0.004356$
Unsystematic Variance of Portfolio $\nu=0.0134\times(0.20)^{2}+0.0225\times(0.50)^{2}+0.0879\times(0.30)^{2}=0.014072.$
Total Variance $=0.00436+0.014072=0.018428$
(iv) Portfolio Variance on the basis of Markowitz Theory
$=(W_{A}\times W_{A}\times{G_{A}}^{2})+(W_{A}\times W_{B}\times Cov_{AB})+(W_{A}\times W_{C}\times Cov_{AC})+(W_{B}\times W_{A}\times Cov_{AB})+$
$(W_{B}\times W_{B}\times\sigma_{B}^{2})+(W_{B}\times W_{c}\times Cov_{Bc})+(W_{c}\times W_{A}\times Cov_{ca})+(W_{c}\times W_{B}\times Cov_{cb})+$
$(W_{c}\times W_{c}\times\sigma_{c}^{2})$
$=(0.20\times0.20\times0.015)+(0.20\times0.50\times0.030)+(0.20\times0.30\times0.020)+(0.20\times0.50\times0.030)$
$+(0.50\times0.50\times0.025)+(0.50\times0.30\times0.040)+(0.30\times0.20\times0.020)+(0.30\times0.50\times0.040)$
$+(0.30\times0.30\times0.10)$
$=0.0363$

Question 10
3 Questions Merged | (8 Marks) Exam Nov 2019
The following are risk and return estimates for two stocks:
The market index has a standard deviation of 25%.
RBI has closed the latest auction for 2500 crores of 182-day T-Bills for the lowest bid of 5.7%, although there
were bidders at a higher rate of 6.3% also for lots of less than 10 crores.
Required:
Calculate the standard deviation of expected returns on stocks A & B.
(i)
(ii)
Which stock is riskier if you are considering them as individual assets (not part of a portfolio)?
(ii)
Suppose a portfolio is to be constructed with the following proportions:
Calculate the expected return, standard deviation of expected return and non-systematic risk (standard
deviation) of the portfolio.
Solution:
(i)
(ii)
From a portfolio risk perspective, B would be considered the riskier stock because it has a larger
$Beta(1.2)$ than $A(0.8)$. When considering each stock individually, a measure of total risk (adjusted for
relative magnitude of expected returns) is appropriate. This measure would be the Coefficient of
Variation. The CV for A is 2.88 $(40.31/14)$. The CV for B is $3(54.08/18)$. Stock B has higher CV indicating
that B is the riskier of the two securities.
(iii) Two risk-free rates are given. The aggressive approach would be to consider 6.3% while the
conservative approach would be to take 5.7%. If we take the moderate value then the simple average
of the two i.e. 6% would be considered as Risk-free rate.
Expected return of the Portfolio $=(0.25\times14)+(0.40\times18)+(0.35\times6)=12.8\%$
Total Risk = Systematic Risk + Unsystematic Risk
Systematic Risk $={\beta_{p}}^{2}\sigma_{M}^{2}$
$\beta_{p}=0.25(0.8)+0.4(1.2)+0.35(0)=0.2+0.48+0=0.68$
Systematic Risk of Portfolio $=\sqrt{(0.68)^{2}\times(25)^{2}}=\sqrt{289}$
Non-systematic Risk of Portfolio
$=(0.25)^{2}\times(35)^{2}+(0.40)^{2}\times(45)^{2}+0=76.56+324=\sqrt{400.56}$
Total Risk $=\sqrt{289+400.56}=26.26\%$

Question 14
4 Questions Merged | Study Material
The following information is available in respect of Security X
You are required to
(a)
determine the Standard Deviation of Market Return and Security Return
(b)
suppose an Investor has 1,00,000 of his personal funds, then how he would construct his portfolio with
Security X so as to achieve expected return of 20% and what will be risk of this portfolio.
(c)
(d)
suppose an investor is invested in Security X with margin of 40% and cost of borrowing is 8% then what
will be the position.
If the risk premium on the market goes up by 2.50% points, what would be the revised expected return
on the stock based on CAPM ?
Solution: (a) First we shall compute the ẞ of Security X.
Risk Free Rate $=\frac{Coupon~Payment}{Current~Market~Price}=\frac{7}{140}=5\%$
Assuming equilibrium return to be equal to CAPM return then:
(i)
$15\%=R_{f}+\beta$ (Rm-Rf)
$15\%=5\%+\beta$ (15%-5%)
$B_{x}=1$
or it can also be computed as follows:
$\frac{R_{m}}{R_{s}}=\frac{15\%}{15\%}=1$
Standard Deviation of Market Return
$\beta_{x}=\frac{cov_{x,m}}{\sigma_{m-}^{2}}=\frac{225\%}{\sigma_{m}^{2}}=1$
$\sigma_{m}^{2}=225$
$\sigma_{m}=15\%$
(ii) Standard Deviation of Security Return
$\beta_{x}=\frac{\sigma_{x}}{\sigma_{m}}\times\rho_{xm}=\frac{\sigma_{x}}{15}\times0.75=1.$
$\sigma_{x}=\frac{15}{0.75}=20\%$
CA, CFA (USA), CPA (USA) PRAVEEN KHATOD - Leaders in Advanced Financial Education Across India
141
Alpha Academy
PORTFOLIO MANAGEMENT
(b) Let Y be the proportion of investment in X then investment in risk-free securities will be (1-Y),
then $120\%=15\%\times(1-Y)$
or $.20=0.15Y+0.05-0.05Y$
or Y = 1.5 or 150%
Thus, borrow 50% of owned fund at risk free rate of interest of 5% which comes to  50000.
Now invest total fund of 150000 in Security X.
Risk of above Portfolio $=20\%\times1.5+0\%\times-0.5=30\%\times-0.5=30\%.$
(c) Where Security X is margined out 40% with cost of borrowing at 8% the position of Expected Return and
risk will be as follows:
$R_{p}=15\%\times1.4+8\%\times(-0.4)=17.8\%$
Risk of above Portfolio $=20\%\times1.4+0\%\times-0.4=28\%.$
(d) Return from Market goes up by 2.5% points i.e. $15\%+2.5\%=17.5\%$
