Question 15
Study Material, Practice Manual, (8 Marks) N 14, M 18, ΜΤΡ Μ 19, MTP N 23, Μ 25
The risk free rate of return Rf is 9 percent. The expected rate of return on the market portfolio Rm is 13
percent. The expected rate of growth for the dividend of Platinum Ltd. is 7 percent. The last dividend paid on
the equity stock of Platinum Ltd was 2.00. The beta of Platinum Ltd. equity stock is 1.2.
(i) What is the equilibrium price of the equity stock of Platinum Ltd.?
(ii) How would the equilibrium price change when
• The inflation premium increases by 2 percent?
The expected growth rate increases by 3 percent?
•
The beta of Platinum Ltd. equity rises to 1.3?
Tutorial Note: In RTP M25, ICAI has
replaced first two "?" by "and" Hence,
the only correct answer will be 35.48
Solution: (i) Equilibrium price of Equity using CAPM
$=9\%+1.2(13\%-9\%)=13.8\%$
$\nu=\frac{D1}{K_{e}-g}=\frac{2.00(1.07)}{0.138-0.07}=\frac{2.14}{0.068}=\overline{7.47}$
(ii)
New Equilibrium price of Equity using CAPM
$=11\%+1.3(15\%-11\%)=16.20\%$
$\nu=\frac{D1}{k_{e}-g}=\frac{2.00(1.10)}{0.162-0.10}=\overline{7}35.48$
Alternatively, if all the factors are taken separately then solution will be as follows:
(i)
(ii)
(iii)
Inflation Premium increase by 2%. This raises Rx to 15.80%. Hence;
new equilibrium price will be:
$=\frac{2.00(1.07)}{0.158-0.07}=\overline{7}24.32$
Expected Growth rate increases by 3%. Hence, revised growth rate stands at 10%:
$=\frac{2.00(1.10)}{0.138-0.10}=\overline{7}57.89$
Beta rises to 1.3. Hence, revised cost of equity shall be:
$=9\%+1.3(13\%-9\%)=14.2\%$
As a result, New Equilibrium price shall be:
$P=\frac{D1}{K_{e}-g}=\frac{2.00(1.07)}{0.142-0.07}=\frac{2.14}{0.068}=\overline{7}29.72$

153
VaR [Value at Risk]
Risk
Management
LDR
Hr
LMR
5 Mins
VaR is a measure of risk of investment. Given the normal market condition in a set of period, say, one
day, it estimates how much an investment might lose. This investment can be a portfolio, capital
investment or foreign exchange etc., VaR answers two basic questions -
(i) What is worst case scenario?
(ii)
What will be the loss?
There are two ingredients required before we calculate VaR
✓ Time frame
✓ Confidence level
Eg. Daily VaR, Weekly VaR, Monthly VaR, Semi Annual VaR, Annual Var etc.
Other things being constant higher the time frame higher would be Value-at-Risk
i.e. probabilities. Eg. generally we calc 1% VaR, 5% VaR, 10% VaR.
Interpretation of VAR
Let's say 5% Daily VaR $=\$40,000$
There are 2 correct interpretations :-
(1) There is a 95% confidence that on any given day maximum loss would be \$40000.
(2) There is only a 5% chance that on any given day losses could be even more than \$ 40000
Calculation of VaR
Z score
i.e. No.
of σ
- 4
- 3
Confidence
Value
at
-Risk
- 2
- 1
0
1
2
3
4
Tutorial Note: Mean return (µ) is generally assumed as 0% while calculating VaR (reason being
VaR is calculated for shorter time frames e.g. Daily, Weekly and in shorterm mean return is ~ 0%)
$\overline{x}=0\%$
$\sigma=4\%$
-16%
-12%
-8%
15.87% chances that
-4%
0%
loss will exceed 4%
4%
84.13% confidence that
max loss will be 4%
8%

2.28% chances that
97.72% confidence that
loss will exceed 8%
max loss will be 8%
0.13% chances that
99.87% confidence that
loss will exceed 12%
max loss will be 12%
Calculating VaR is exactly reverse process of what we have studied in portfolio management

Step 1 $Z=-1.645$
↓
Step2% or loss amount
Step 1: Find Z score corresponding to the given confidence / probability. eg 5% VaR translates into 95%
confidence
It is corresponding to the area of 0.45, the Z no. is -1.645 (refer Normal Distribution curve table)
At 95% probability $z=1.645$ [by looking at the probability table (0.45)]
Step 2: Calc VaR
here,
Max loss or VaR, = Investment amount $\times\sigma_{d}\%\times\sqrt{t}\times Z$ score
to convert volatility/
Deviation% in to terms
to stretch daily

On any day we are 95% confident that loss will not exceed 6580.
There is a 5% chance that losses may exceed 6580 on any particular day.

RISK MANAGEMENT
Example: A trader at Goldman sachs is analysing a trading opportunity & plans to place an order worth \$20,00,000
The Daily standard deviation of the position is \$80000. Maximum tolerance limit of loss for this trader can be
\$ 150000 on daily basis with 99% confidence. Calculate 1% daily VAR
Solve:
Step 1 At 1% probability of loss, (ie at 99% confidence level) corresponding z no is -2.33
Step 2 Max Loss $=\sigma_{d}\times\sqrt{t}\times z$
$=80000\times\sqrt{1}\times2.33=\$186400$
hence, 1% daily VaR is \$ 186400
Step 3 Interpretation of VaR
!
Caution Note:
Always pay attention to time frame of
 before calculating VaR
1% daily VaR of \$186400 means on any given day there is a 99% confidence that losses will not
exceed \$186400
On other hand there is a just 1% chance that losses might exceed \$186400
Decision: Since VaR (\$ 186400) exceeds tolerance limit (\$ 150000)... order could not be placed. In this case
trader may cut down the position size
Q Calc maximum position size that a trader can place order for?

here, t means desired time frame at which VaR needs to be converted. eg. to calc 20 days VaR
using 1 Day VaR, the value $of\sqrt{t}$ twill be $\sqrt{20}.$

RISK MANAGEMENT
Question 1 2 Questions Merged, Study Material, (4 Marks) Exam Nov 19, MTP May 25, Jan 26
Consider a portfolio consisting of $a=200,00,000$ investment in share XYZ and $a=200,00,000$ investment in
share ABC. The daily standard deviation of both shares is 1% and that the coefficient of correlation between
them is 0.3. You are required to determine the 10- day 99% value at risk for the portfolio?
Also find out the benefit of diversification in terms of VaR.
Solution: The standard deviation of the daily change in the investment in each asset is 2,00,000 i.e. 2 lakhs.
The variance of the portfolio's daily change is
$v=2^{2}+2^{2}+2\times0.3\times2\times2=10.4$
σ (Standard Deviation) = 10.4 = 3.22 lakhs
Accordingly, the standard deviation of the 10-day change is
3.22 lakhs x 10 = 10.18 lakh
From the Normal Table we see that z score for 1% is 2.33. This means that 1% of a normal distribution lies more
than 2.33 standard deviations below the mean. The 10-day 99 percent value at risk is therefore
Benefit of diversification
2.33×10.18 lakh =
Daily $\sigma_{xY2}\&\sigma_{ABC}=\exists20000~each$
23.72 lakh
10 days $\sigma_{xy7}\&\sigma_{ABC}=\mp200000\times\sqrt{10}=\mp632455~each$
10 days 99% $laR=2.33\times8632455\times2~stocks$
= 29.47 lakh
... Benefit of diversification in terms of VaR = 29.47 lakh - 23.72 lakh

$=\%5.75~lakh$

ii Format to calculate Closing NAV using Opening NAV
Expense Ratio or Management Expense Ratio (MER)
It is the age of Assets of MF that were spent to operate a MF
It includes Operating expenses such as Office Exps, Rent, Staff, Salary, Management & advisory fee,
Travel Costs & consultancy fees etc.
It excludes Brokerage Cost for Trading the Portfolio
$Expense~Ratio=\frac{Tota|Expenses}{Average~Tota|NAV}\times100~or\frac{Expenses~per~unit}{(NAV_{o}+NAV_{i})/2}\times100.$

Active Returns
C
MF Performance Evaluation
[aka Tracking Difference]
is the Average of difference in Returns from MF as compared to the Returns from Benchmark Index.
Active Returns $=R_{p}$ less RB
Tracking Error
can be defined as the divergence or deviation of a fund's returns from the Benchmark it is
following.
$TE=\sqrt{\frac{\Sigma(d-\overline{d})^{2}}{n-1}}$
here,
$d=$ Differential return (Return on mutual fund - Return on benchmark)
$\overline{d}=$ Average differential return
$[\frac{\Sigma d}{n}]$
$n=$ No. of observation
Information Ratio
Active Returns earned per unit of Tracking Error
Average Active Returns
=
Tracking Error
Example
Avg Active Return
Tracking Error
$\overline{(d})=\frac{6.3\%}{5}=1.26\%$
$=\sqrt{\frac{\Sigma(d-\overline{d})^{2}}{n-1}}$
$=\sqrt{\frac{28.752}{5-1}}$
$=\sqrt{7.188}=2.68\%$
Information ratio $=\frac{1.26\%}{2.68\%}=0.47$

Question 3
MUTUAL FUNDS
Study Material, (8 Marks) Exam May 06, Nov 18, Sep 25, MTP Sep 22, Nov 23, Jan 26
A Mutual Fund having 300 units has shown its NAV of 8.75 and 9.45 at the beginning and at the end of the
year respectively. The Mutual Fund has given two options:
a. Pay 0.75 per unit as dividend and 0.60 per unit as a capital gain, or
b. These distributions are to be reinvested at an average NAV of 8.65 per unit.
What difference it would make in terms of return available and which option is preferable?
Solution:
Option 1: When Dividend and Capital Gain are paid:
Calculation of monthly return on the mutual funds:
$r=\frac{(NAV_{t}-NAV_{t1})+l_{t}+CG_{t}}{NAV_{t1}}\times100=\frac{(\mathbb{\pi}9.45-\mathbb{8}8.75)+\mathbb{8}0.75+\mathbb{8}0.60}{8.75}\times100=\frac{0.70+1.35}{8.75}=23.43\%$
Option 2: When Dividend and Capital Gain are reinvested:
If all dividends and capital gain are reinvested into additional units at 8.65 per unit the position would be.
Total amount reinvested = 1.35 x 300 = 405
Additional units added $=\frac{\overline{7}405}{8.65}=46.82~unit.$
Value of units at the end = 346.82 units x 9.45 = 3277.45
Price paid for 300 units at the beginning $=(300\times\mp8.75)=\overline{7}2,625$
$Return=(\vec{r}3277.45-\vec{r}2625)/\vec{r}2625=24.85\%$
Conclusion: Since the holding period reward is more in percentage terms in Option 2 i.e. Reinvestment of
distributions at an average NAV of 8.65 per unit this option is preferable.

(ii) Calculation Beta
(a) D Mutual Fund Ltd.

$E(R)-R_{f}=22.50$
Treynor Ratio $=15=\frac{E(R)-R_{i}}{\beta_{0}}=\frac{16.50}{\beta_{0}}$
$\beta_{D}=22.50/15=1.50$
(iii) Decrease in the Value of Equity
(b) K Mutual Fund Ltd.
Sharpe Ratio $=3.3=\frac{E(R)-R_{\prime}}{\sigma_{\kappa}}=\frac{E(R)-R_{\prime}}{5}$
$E(R)-R_{f}=16.50$
Treynor Ratio $=15=\frac{E(R)-R_{r}}{\beta_{\kappa}}=\frac{16.50}{\beta_{\kappa}}$
$\beta_{k}=16.50/15=1.10$

(ii) (1)
Let N be the opening NAV, then
$N(1+0.25)=\overline{7}24.95$
N = 19.96
i.e., beginning NAV = 19.96
(2)
Let X be the number of units purchased
Then ending units $=20,800$
Accordingly,
$20800=x+\frac{0.998X}{24.95}$
$20800=\frac{24.95X+0.998X}{24.95}$
$X=20000$
Thus, number of units to be purchased $=20,000$

If Face Value of Bond is not given then assume it as 100 or 1000 as appropriate.
If Redemption Price is not given then assume redemption at Par (irrespective of whether Issue is at a

If Bond makes semi-annual coupon payments, then
Convert Annual coupon rate to Semi-annual rate [by dividing it by 2]
Convert Discounting rate to Semi-annual rate [by dividing it by 2]
Convert No. of yrs to maturity to No. of semi-annual periods [by multiplying it by 2]

Bond Yield
Bond yield is the return an investor will earn if he purchases the bond on its issue date & holds the bond
until its maturity
Alt1:
1.
Accurate Approach
Use IRR
Alt2: Shortcut or Approximate Approach
$=\frac{I+\frac{RP-IP}{n\cdot\epsilon}}{\frac{RP+IP}{2\cdot here,DP}}$
Life of the bond
means Redemption price
IP means Issue price
If bond is both issued & redeemed at par then Bond yield% = Coupon rate%
Exam Tip
Although very rare, but if Q asks to calculate Post-tax Yield or Post-tax Returns then -
In IRR method, we should write Post-tax Cashflows.
In Shortcut method, use $I(1-t)$ and deduct Capital Gains Tax amount from RP.
2. If Q is silent then prefer 'Accurate approach' i.e. IRR in exams
Above exam tips are equally applicable for below varieties of Yield's as well.

Caution Note: Don't make the mistake of using Fair Price in the
denominator. The correct denominator is Market Price.
Current yield is an incomplete form of return. It ignores price appreciation%.
To find complete return% over 1 year period, we use Total Yield%
Total yield % = Current yield % + Price Appreciation%

However, it may not always be possible to reinvest CF's at the same rate as IRR. Hence, if reinvestment
rate is different from IRR we use the concept of MIRR.
Calc MIRR if reinvestment rate is 15% instead of 24.89%?
Steps to calculate MIRR or RYTM
1. Calculate 'Future Value on Maturity date' of Intermediate Cf's @ Reinvestment Rate%
2. Now Use $FV=PV(1+r)^{n}$ to find 'r'. The 'r' so calculated is MIRR or RYTM.

Conversion Premium
means 'Premium' over Conversion value' that people are ready to pay for purchasing a Convertible bond.
Convertible bond commands premium because of two features :-
(i) Limited downside risk as compared to Eq. shares
(ii) Coupon Rate% > Dividend Yield % (usually)

$=(MP-E)\times n$

$E=$ Exercise Price of Warrant

Risks
Inflation Risk - refers to the rise in the price of products and the consequent fall in
the value of money.
E
Types of Risk
(1
 2
3
Interest Rate Risk (aka Price Risk) - refers to the impact that rising interest rates
have on bond values. When interest rates go up, the value of an existing bond comes
down & vice-versa.
Reinvestment Risk - Risk that intermediate CF's cannot be reinvested @ IRR of the
Original Bond.
Liquidity Risk - Loss of Value at the time of en-cashing the Bond before its maturity
4
5
Credit Risk / Default Risk - Possibility that issuer goes bankrupt

Yield%
Bond Price-Yield relationship is a convex shape
relationship. By convex shape we mean that
✓ when YTM decreases, bond price increases but
at a higher pace.
on the contrary when YTM increases then bond
price decreases but at a slower pace.
A Zero coupon bond having maturity after 5 years.

$1000=620(1+r)^{5}$
$r=10.03$% i.e $YTM=10.03\%$.

Observe that the change in price is different in both the directions.
Now let's measure risk i.e. by how much price changes due to change in interest rates by calculating volatility.
Duration & Modified Duration/ Volatility%
Measurement of risk is done by calculating volatility.
Volatility means by how much the bond price will change for every 1% change in YTM [i.e. every 1%
change in prevailing interest rates in the economy]

Yield%
Ideally, we should measure slope of curve to get the accurate answers, however it is difficult to measure
slope of curve... we use a work around by dropping a tangent line at present YTM level. Now we measure slope
of the tangent line ignoring convexity feature. The slope of this tangent line is called as volatility.
$=\frac{2.78\%+2.67\%}{2}=2.725\%$
.. Bond prices will change by 2.725% for every 0.60% $\Delta$ (change) in interest rate.
However, volatility is measured w.r.t. 1% change in interest rates (NOT0.60%)
Δin ΥΤΜ%
0.60%
... 1%
Bond Price
$\Delta in$
2.275%
$?=2.725\%\times\frac{1\%}{0.60\%}=4.54\%$
Interpretation of Volatility
Bond prices will change by 4.54% for every 1% change in YTM [i.e. change in market interest rates /
prevailing interest rate in the economy] in the opposite direction.
Alternatively above calculation of volatility can also be done by using effective duration formula:
Effective Duration $=\frac{V_{.}-V_{.}}{2\times V_{0}\times\Delta y}$
This formula has been derived using logic already taught above
here, $V_{0}$ means bond current prices; V. & V. means New Bond price when YTM is decreased & increased
respectively.
$\Delta_{Y}$ means change in YTM
$=\frac{637.26-603.44}{2\times620\times0.60}=4.54\%$

$=\frac{V_{.}-V_{.}}{2\times V_{0}\times\Delta y}$

For a 1% $\Delta$ in YTM, Bond price will change by 3.71%
For a 2% $\Delta$ in YTM, Bond price will change by $3.71\%\times2=7.42\%$
Macaulay Duration (or simply say 'duration') of the bond is the Weighted average maturity of its cash flow
structure, where present value of CFs discounted at current Y TM are assigned as weights.
Step to calculate Duration of bond
Step 1: Find expected cash flow from Bond in each year
Step 2: Calculate present value of each year cash flow using YТМ.
Σ PV of CF's = Market price of bond
Step 3: Calculate Weight of present value of cash flow of each year
PV of cash flow of each year
Σ PV of cash flows
Step 4: Year x Weight of PV of cash flow of each year
' Year x Weight' becomes Duration of bond
Format for calculation of duration of bond:

Bond selection decision
↑
Decision Making using the concept of duration
Duration of Bond Portfolio
is weighted average duration of individual bonds where market values are the assigned weights.
Duration of bonds portfolio = ∑Duration x W
Weights are Market Value weights
A
Caution Note Don't make the mistake of using Face Value, Market Price per Bond or No. of
Bonds as Weights. The correct Weight is Market Value of Bonds in the portfolio
If Question provides you Bonds Portfolio Duration and asks for churning advice given the expected
change in Interest Rates then simply follow the above taught concept of Bonds selection. It means
✓ If Interest Rates are expected to rise, then advise Selling some Long Duration Bonds and Invest
the proceeds in Short Duration Bonds so as to reduce Overall Duration of Bonds Portfolio.
✓ If Interest Rates are expected to lower, then advise Buying Long Duration Bonds by Selling some
Short Duration Bonds so as to increase Overall Duration of Bonds Portfolio.

We know that price yield curve is

duration (volatility) is the slope of the
straight line. The discrepancies between
the price yield curve & the modified
duration increases with the bigger
changes in interest rates. The process of
correcting the gap between the modified
duration and convex price yield curve is
called as 'Convexity Adjustment'.

A 2yrs, 8% coupon bond having F.V. \$ 1000 is trading at $YTM=10\%$, calculate convexity &
find out new price of the bond for 1% change in YTM in either direction.
Step 1: Calculate Macaulay Duration
Duration
$=\frac{\Sigma WD}{\Sigma W}=\frac{1857.85}{965.29}=1.9247~Years$
Step2: Calculate Convexity
Modified duration i.e. volatility
$=\frac{Duration}{1+YTM}=\frac{1.9247}{1+0.10}=1.75.$
Years or 1.75%
Calc of V+ & V- (Assuming interest rate shock of 1% is given)
Convexity
$=\frac{V_{.}+V_{.}-2V_{0}}{2\times V_{0}\times(\Delta Y)^{2}}$
$=\frac{982.41+948.62-2\times965.29}{2\times965.29\times(1\%)^{2}...}=2.33$
Step 3: Convexity Adjustment
$=Convexity\times100\times\Delta Y^{2}$
$=2.33\times100\times(1\%)^{2}/$
$=0.0233\%$
Take it in decimal form, $1\%=0.01$
hence $(1\%)^{2}$ means $(0.01)^{2}=0.0001$
On Calculator write 1% as 0.01
Since we have already multiplied by 100 above hence
answer will be in % terms

200
Alpha Academy
MANAGEMENT OF BONDS PORTFOLIO
Step 4 & 5: % Change in Bond Price & New MP of the Bond
!
Conclusion: Applying only 'Volatility %' gives us Approx New MP of Bond
Applying 'Volatility $\%\pm$ Convexity Adjustment %' gives us Accurate New MP of Bond
When does Convexity Adjustment should be added to Volatility% & when deducted?
Since Price-Yield Curve is a convex shape, bond price rises at a higher pace when YTM decreases,
accordingly CA% should be added to Volatility % when yield decreases.
On the contrary, the bond price falls at a lower pace when YTM increases, accordingly CA% should be
deducted from Volatility% when yield increases.
Caution Note Delta $\Delta Y$ comes at 2 places, once in convexity formula & next time in convexity adj.
formula. Remember that both $\triangle Y$ are different.
$\triangle Y$
in Convexity formula here $\triangle Y$ means' Quantam of interest rate shock given' to find out V+ & V-.
It is at our discretion how much shock we want to give (usually less than 1%)
$\triangle Y$ in Convexity Adjustment formula this is actual / expected change in YTM (Usually given in the
question) corresponding to which New market price is to be found.
Exam Tip: We can use same Ay at both the places. In other words we will give discretionary shock same
as change in Y TM given in the question.

Bond Immunization
MANAGEMENT OF BONDS PORTFOLIO
Bond Immunization is an Investment strategy used to minimize Interest Rate Risk & Reinvestment
Rate Risk. It is done by adjusting Bond's Portfolio Duration so as to match with Investor's Liabilities
due dates.
Immunization locks-in a fixed rate of return or yield %
I must buy a
New house in 6
yrs from now
$D_{A}=D_{L}$
So an investor needs to buy Bonds having duration $=6$ yrs. but it may
not be practically possible for all the bonds to have duration $=6$ yrs.
Hence, an investor will buy bonds of different duration but in such a
weight proportion so that overall Duration of Bond Portfolio $=6$ years. In
other words Bonds Investment horizon is matched with liability horizon.
6thyr
You need to
make payment
to buy house
Set
Bond
Portfolio
Duration
$=6$

$Duration_{A}\times Weight_{A}+Dur_{B}\times W_{B}+Dur_{c}\times W_{c}.$
$*here,Weight_{A}+Weight_{s}+Weight_{c}=1$
1. How to calc "Amount to be invested initially in each Bond" on the basis of weights calculated above

2.
3.
Step 2: Amount to be invested in each Bond = PV of Liab x Weight of Bond as calc above.
If on some future date, Duration of Bond changes (for whatever reason) then we need to calculate
Revised Weights for each of the Bond so as to match $D_{L}$
If Q gives info about Liabilities spreaded over multiple period then first calc W.A. $D_{L}$ i.e. weighted
Avg. Duration of liabilities in the same way as we calc Duration of an individual Bond. Hence calc
PV of such Liabilities & use them as weights to multiply by 'Year in which liability is due'. If Q gives
only a single liability which is due in say, 6 years, then there is no need to apply the concept of PV. 6
yrs itself will be the $D_{L}$.

Money Market Instruments
Money market is a market for trading in short term securities viz Treasury Bills, Commercial Bills,
Commercial Papers & Certificate of deposit. These instruments are front- ended negotiable instrument,
issued at a discount and redeemed at face value.
Face value = 100; $t=6$ months; Rate of discount = 20% pa
EXAMPLE
Solve: Discount
$=\mp100\times20\%\times\frac{6}{12}=\mp10.$
Issue Price or sales value $=\mathbb{F}100-\mathbb{F}10=\mathbb{F}90$
Effective yield $\%=\frac{FV-SV}{SV}\times\frac{365~05~12}{n}\times100=\frac{100-90}{90}\times\frac{12}{6}\times100=22.22\%.$
Cost of funds [raised through Commercial Paper (CP)
$=\frac{[Interest~Expense+Issue~Expense](1-t)}{Net~Amount~received~by~the~company}\times\frac{12~or~365}{n}\times100.$
here, Interest Expense = Face value - Issue price
t = Tax rate
Net amount received by the company = Issue Price - Issue Expenses - Minimum balance to be
maintained in Bank

ABC Ltd. issued 9%, 5 year bonds of 1,000/- each having a remaining maturity of 3 years. The present rate of
interest is 12% for one year tenure. It is expected that Forward rate of interest for one year tenure is going to
fall by 75 basis points and further by 50 basis points for every next year in further for the same tenure. This
bond has a beta value of 1.02 and is more popular in the market due to less credit risk.
Calculate
(i)
Intrinsic value of bond
(ii)
Expected price of bond in the market
(iii)
Interpret the nature of the above yield curve and reasons for the same.
Solution: (i) Intrinsic value of Bond
PV of Interest + PV of Maturity Value of Bond
Forward rate of interests
PV of interest
$=\frac{90}{(1+0.12)}+\frac{90}{(1+0.12)(1+0.1125)}+\frac{90}{(1+0.12)(1+0.1125)(1+0.1075)}=217.81.$
PV of Maturity Value of Bond
1000
$I=\frac{7}{(1+0.12)(1+0.1125)(1+0.1075)}=724.67\\ 81+724.67=\mathbb{7}947.48\end{aligned}$
Intrinsic value of Bond = 217.81
(ii)
(iii)
Expected Price = Intrinsic Value x Beta Value $=\mathbb{\times}942.48\times1.02=\mathbb{\times}961.33$
The given yield curve is inverted yield curve.
The main reason for this shape of curve is expectation for forthcoming recession when investors are
more interested in short term rates over the long term.

(b)
If the current interest rate is 8%, the company will not extend the duration of Bond and the maximum

$=\pm1,000\times PV|AF(8\%,6)+E~10,000\times PV|F$ (8%, 6)
$=f~1,000\times4.623+\underline{10,000\times0.630$

$=f~1,000\times PV|AF(12\%,6)+f~10,000\times PV|F(12\%,6)$
$=\{1,000\times4.111+f~10,000\times0.507$
$=f9,181$

Find the current market price of a bond having face value 1,00,000 redeemable after 6 year maturity with
YTM at 16% payable annually and duration 4.3202 years. Given $1.16^{6}=2.4364.$
Solution: Let the interest Amount be x
Caln of Duration
Duration
$=\frac{\Sigma WD}{\Sigma W}$
$=>4.3202=\frac{246264+11.3225x}{41044+3.6847x}$
(@YTM%, nth Year)
here, Y means YTM
T means Maturity Period
C means Coupon Rate
.. x = 15049 ~ 15000 [... Coupon Rate = 15%]
MP = Interest x PVPIF
+ Redemption Price x PVF
(@YTM%, n Yrs)
$=\boxed{\times}15000\times PVAF_{(\odot16\%,6~vears)}+\mathbb{\times}100000\times PVF_{(\odot16\%,6th~veat)}$
= 96315
Alternative Solution
$Duration=\frac{1+Y}{Y}-\frac{(1+Y)+T(C-Y)}{C[(1+Y)^{T}-1]+Y}$
$4.3202=\frac{1.16}{0.16}-\frac{1.16+6(C-0.16)}{C[(1.16)^{6}-1]+0.16}$
$4.3202=7.25-\frac{1.16+6C-0.96}{1.4364C+0.16}.$
$\frac{0.20+6C}{.4364C+0.16}=2.9298$
$\Rightarrow4.2083C+0.4687=0.20+6C$
$\Rightarrow0.2687=1.7917C$
.. $C=0.14996\approx0.15$ or 15%

Question 11
3 Questions Merged | Study Material, (6 Marks) Exam N15, N18, RTP N21, M25, МТР М21
Mr. A will need 1,00,000 after two years for which he wants to make one time necessary investment now. He
has a choice of two types of bonds. Their details are as below:
(i)
Advice Mr. A whether he should invest all his money in one type of bond or he should buy both the bonds
and, if so, in which quantity?
Assume that there will not be any call risk or default risk.
(ii)
State the condition to be fulfilled for perfect immunization.
(iii)
After the portfolio has been formulated, an interest rate change occurs, increasing the yield to 11%. The
new duration of these bonds are: Bond $X=1$ Year and Bond $Y=3.546$ years. Is the portfolio still
immunized? Why or why not
(iv) Determine the new percentage of X and Y bonds that are needed to immunize the portfolio.
CA, CFA (USA), CPA (USA) PRAVEEN KHATOD - Leaders in Advanced Financial Education Across India
213
Alpha Academy
Solution:
(i)
MANAGEMENT OF BONDS PORTFOLIO
Duration of Bond X
Duration of the Bond is 1 year
Duration of Bond Y
Duration of the Bond Y is 3.563 years
Let X be the investment in Bond X and therefore investment in Bond Y shall be $(1-X)$. Since the required
duration is 2 year the proportion of investment in each of these two securities shall be computed as follows:
$2=X\times1+(1-X)\times3.563$
$X=0.61$
Accordingly, the proportion of investment shall be 61% in Bond X and 39% in Bond Y respectively.
Amount of investment
Note: The investor has to keep the money invested for two years. Therefore, the investor can invest in
both the bonds with the assumption that Bond X will be reinvested for another one year on same returns.
(ii) Assumption for perfect immunization:
(a) Yield curve is flat
(b)
(c)
Interest Rate changes are Parallel shifts up or down in the yield curve.
Duration of Asset & liability remains unchanged
(iii) With revised yield the Revised Duration of Bond Portfolio stands at
$0.61\times1~year+0.39\times3.546~year=1.9929~years$
No, Portfolio is not immunized as the duration of the portfolio has been decreased from 2 years to
1.9929 years.
(iv) New percentage of X and Y bonds that are needed to immunize the portfolio
Let proportion of investment in Bond X and Y is x and 1-x respectively, then
$1x+3.546(1-x)=2$
$x=0.6072$
Accordingly, the % of investment of X and Y is 60.72% and 39.28% respectively

crore. Assuming that clean price be 99.42 and initial Margin be 2% and days of accrued interest be 262 days.

(iv)
Suppose repo rate & clean price are not given in the Q how could you find using rest of the info & addl.
info obtained in points answered above
Under the arrangement entered by bank A and bank B who is borrowing & who is lending and for whom
the transaction repo & reverse repo?
Solution:
(i)
Dirty Price = Clean Price + Interest Accrued
$=99.42+100\times\frac{10}{100}\times\frac{262}{360}=106.70$
(ii) First Leg (Start Proceed)
= Nominal Value $\times\frac{DirtyPrice}{100}\times\frac{100-|nitial~Margin}{100}$
$=\mathbb{7}8,00,000\times\frac{106.72}{100}\times\frac{100-2}{100}=\mathbb{7}8,36,52,800$
Second Leg (Repayment at Maturity)
$=Start~Proceed\times(1+Repo~rate\times\frac{No.of~days}{360})$
$=\mathbb{7}8,36,52,800\times(1+0.0565\times\frac{14}{360})=\mathbb{7}8,38,36,604.$
(iii) Calculation of Repo Rate
$Second~Leg=Start~Proceed\times(1+Repo~Rate\times\frac{No.of~days}{360}).$
$\mathbb{7}8,38,36,604=\mathbb{7}8,36,52,800\times(1+Repo~Rate\times\frac{14}{360})$
$1.002197=(1+Repo~Rate\times\frac{14}{360})$
Repo Rate $=0.0565=5.65\%$
Calculation of Dirty Price
Repo means Repurchase transaction.
In a repo, one party sells an Asset
(usually fixed income securities) to
another party at one price & commits to
repurchase the same from second party
at a different price at a future date. The
assets, therefore, acts as a collateral &
mitigates credit risk.
$irst~Leg(Start~Proceed)=Nominal~Value\times\frac{DirtyPrice}{100}\times\frac{100-|nitial~Margin}{100}$
$78,36,52,800=7~8,00,00,000\times\frac{Dirty~Price}{100}\times\frac{100-2}{100}$
$1.04566=\frac{Dirty~Price}{100}\times\frac{100-2}{100}$ ... Dirty Price = 106.70
(iv) Bank A is borrowing & hence a repo transaction for bank A.
Bank B is landing & hence a reverse repo transaction for bank B.

Derivatives ?
Basic Building Blocks
Derivatives are financial instruments that derive their value from the value of an underlying asset.
Underlying assets could be stocks, currency, gold, bonds, commodities etc.
Forward
Futures
Options
Swaps & Interest Rate
Derivatives
{Covered as a separate chapter}
A forward contract is a customized contract under which one party agrees to buy and the other party
agrees to sell a specified asset on a specified future date at a price agreed upon today.
A futures contract is a standardized contract under which one party agrees to buy and the other
party agrees to sell a specified asset on a specified future date at a price agreed upon today. In other
words, futures are exchange-traded forward contracts.
An option is a contract between two parties under which the buyer of an option buys the right, and not
the obligation, to buy or sell a specified quantity of certain underlying asset at or before pre-
determined date at a price agreed upon today.
Forward vs Futures
CA, CFA (USA), CPA (USA) PRAVEEN KHATOD - Leaders in Advanced Financial Education Across India

Alpha Academy
Time Value of Money
Discrete Compounding
If Comp freq. is given
$FV=PV(1+r)^{n}$
If Comp freq. is not given
$FV=PV(1+r\times\frac{n}{12})$
DERIVATIVES ANALYSIS & VALUATION
Continuous Compounding
$FV=PV\times e^{rt}$
here, e means exponential value $[e=2.71828]$
r means rate of interest compounded continuously
Always use per annum rate in place of 'r'
 means time period (in n/12 or n/365 format)
IF PV = 100, $n=3$ months, $r=12\%$ Calculate FV under below situations:
EXAMPLE
(i) If comp freq is given
(ii) If $r=12$% pa (Comp freq not given)
(a)
$r=12\%$ pa comp annually
(iii) If $r=12\%$ pa compounded continuously.
(b)
$r=12^{\circ}$% pa comp quarterly
Solve: (i)
$=100(1+0.12)^{3/12.years}$
(ii) $FV=100(1+0.12\times\frac{3}{12})$
$=103$
(iii) $FV=100\times e^{0.12\times3/12}$
$=100\times e^{0.03}$
$=102.87$
$=100\times1.03045$
$=103.045$
$=103$
(a) $FV=PV(1+r)^{n}$
(b) $FV=100(1+0.03)^{1~Qtr}$
Types of Margin
1. Initial Margin is required to be deposited at the time of initiation of the contract.
2.
Initial Margin $=\mu+3\sigma$ or Contract value x Initial margin%
here, umeans Average daily absolute change
σmeans Standard Deviation of daily price Changes
Example: The average daily absolute change of Reliance Industries shares is 60 and standard
deviation of these changes is 25. Then Initial Margin $=\mp135$ per share $[\mp60+3\times\mp25].$ If 1 Lot has
300 shares of Reliance, then Initial Margin per lot $=\mathbb{F}135\times300=\mathbb{F}40500$
Mark - to market margin [MTM] takes care of daily gain / losses. The party who incurs loss makes the
Payment which is then passed on to the other party who made gains.
Daily MTM = (Δin closing futures price of today vs. previous day) x Lot size x No. of lots
Maintenance Margin
3.
→ Initial Margin = 100000
As soon as you breach the
Loss
No Margin Call
maintenance level, you have
to re-fill it back upto the
Loss
initial margin level
Maintenance Margin = 60000
4.
Additional Margin When Exchange predicts higher volatility ahead then it calls for Addl. margin which
is in addition to the Initial margin so as to cover the additional risk posed by major events such as
Election results etc.

ARBITRAGE
Arbitrage is a two-sided tr™
entered into at the same time to
earn risk-free arbitrage gains due
to mispricing in market
Tutorial Note
Speculation in Forward/ Futures may
result into either gain/ loss depending
upon the movement of share prices.
Arbitrage
is the process of buying a security in one market and simultaneously selling an equal product in another
market to profit from pricing differences. Hence, a two-step process is followed:
Step 1 Calculate Fair Futures Prices
Step 2 If Fair Futures Price  Actual Futures Price then arbitrage opportunity exists. To earn profits simply
enter into following actions:
(a) Buy Undervalued Instrument,
(b) Sell the Other instrument &
(c) Borrow/Invest an appropriate amount (to fund above transactions)

General Points to Remember
DERIVATIVES ANALYSIS & VALUATION
If Q only gives rate of intt say 12% p.a. & doesn't specify anything about compounding freq. then treat
12% pa as a simple interest rate.
2.
Contango & Backwardation Market situations:
Basis = Spot Price - Future Price
If Basis is Positive
↓
Backwardation Market
If Basis is Negative
↓
Contango Market
3. If Actual Futures Price > Theoretical Future Price then Future is Overpriced.
Action: Short Future, Long Spot & Borrow {it is called as Cash & Carry Arbitrage}
If Actual Future Price < Theoretical Future Price then Future is Underpriced.
Action: Long Future, Short Spot & Invest {it is called as Reverse Cash & Carry Arbitrage}
4. Settlement of futures contract
Two modes
5.
By Price Difference
i.e. pay/ receive the Difference $b/w$
Futures price agreed originally vs.
spot price prevailing on the due date
Index Future are always settled
by price difference since an
Index cannot be delivered in spot
↓
By Actual delivery
i.e. actually Buy / Sell share @
originally agreed futures price
If Q is silent about mode of settlement & Future
price on expiry date is not given in the Q, then
settle Stock future contract through delivery.
Tutorial Note: Irrespective of the mode of settlement,
final arbitrage gain amount remains the same, usually!
Default assumptions:
If settlement on expire date - By actual delivery
If squaring off positions before expire date - By price difference
Convergence of Futures price & Spot price on expiry date.
Gold futures price
 160500
 160000
Today
Gold spot price
Time
+
Due date
Ideally futures price on the last
date should exactly equal spot price
on last date.
However, practically there could be
some minor differences. Hence, if in
exam actual futures price on the due
date is given then use it to square
off the transaction else use spot
price on the due date.

How to find equivalent rates continuous
Continuous to Normal
$r_{1}=m\times(e^{\frac{r_{2}}{m}}-1)$
DERIVATIVES ANALYSIS & VALUATION
Normal
here, r₁ means Normal rate
r₂ means Continuous rate
m means No. of compoundings in a year
Eg. 12% pa continuously compounded.
Calc equivalent rate if compounded semi- ann
Solve: $r_{1}=m\times(e^{r2/m}-1)$
EXAMPLE
$=2\times(e^{0.12/2}-1)$
$=2\times(e^{0.06}-1)$
$=2\times(1.06184-1)$
$=12.368\%$ pa comp semi-annually
Normal to Continuous
$r_{2}=m\times Ln(1+\frac{r_{1}}{m})$
Eg. If 12.368% pa compounded semi- annually is the
rate then calc equivalent continuously comp rate.
$r_{2}^{Solve:=2\times Ln(1+\frac{0.12368}{2})$
$=2\times Ln(1.06184)$
$=2\times0.06$
$=0.12$ i.e. 12% pра сс
[Source: ICAI Study Material, RTP May 2024]
The price of ACC stock on 31 December 2024 was
stock on the same date, i.e., 31 December 2024 for March 2025 was
220 and the futures price on the same
230. Other information:
Evaluate arbitrage opportunity if any?
Solve: Step 1 Calculate fair future price
Fair future price $=220+(220\times0.15\times0.25)-(0.25\times\mp10)=225.75$
Step 2 Compare future prices (Fair v/s actual) & evaluate arbitrage opportunity.
Since Fair futures price (225.75) < Actual future price (230), future contract are overvalued. This would
give rise to arbitrage opportunities.
An arbitrageur should:
(i) Buy the ACC stock at 220
(ii) Sell the March 2025 futures on ACC stock.
(iii) Borrow the amount of 220@15% for a period of 3 months and
By 31st March 2025, he will receive the dividend of 2.50 per share.
On the expiry date of 31st March, he will deliver the ACC stock against the March futures contract sales.
The arbitrager's inflows/outflows are as follows:
Thus, the arbitrager earns 4.25 per share without involving any risk.

Q. What if in above case ACC futures were trading @222 instead of 230.
Step 1 Same as above
Step 2 Since Fair futures price (225.75) < Actual future price (222), future contract are undervalued.
This would give rise to arbitrage opportunities.
An arbitrageur should:
(i)
Sell the ACC stock at
220 (by borrowing stock under SLBS scheme)
(ii)
Invest the amount of
220 @ 15% for a period of 3 months and
(iii) Buy the March 2025 futures on ACC stock.
By 31st March 2025, he will need to pay the dividend of 2.50 per share.
On the expiry date of 31st March, he will receive the ACC Stock under future contract and deliver the same
under SLBS scheme.
The arbitrager's inflows/outflows are as follows:
Thus, the arbitrager earns 3.75 per share without involving any risk.

Meaning of Convenience Yield
DERIVATIVES ANALYSIS & VALUATION
One who buys commodity in spot also enjoys the convenience of consuming/ using such commodity in
times of need. But this convenience is not enjoyed by Futures Contract buyer, hence he'll deduct amt
for Conv Yield.
Exam Tip: If Convenience Yield is given in terms instead of % terms, then formula changes to:
$F=(So+S-I-C)\times e^{rt}$
here, C means PV of Convenience Yield amount
Miscellaneous aspects

Mathematics of Ln(x)
DERIVATIVES ANALYSIS & VALUATION
Just like Antilog is opposite of Log, similarly Ln is opposite of ex.
It means if you take some number say 'x', then calc ex, then calc Ln (ex), you'll get 'x' again.

$CMP=\mp300$

Concept 1: Hedging a stock - Using stock futures
EXAMPLE
Suppose you hold 9600 shares of ITC @ 450. Now you expect a sudden fall in share price.
How can you protect your long position?
Simply enter into Opposite Action in Future Contract
i.e. If Long in Spot then go Short in Future contract or If Short in spot then go Long in future contract for the
same no. of shares.
Proof: If shares of ITC falls by 10%, show how are you protected?
Spot Position
Long in Spot on ITC shares
@ 450
10%
 405
Loss in spot $=$ per share x 9600 shares
= ( 432000)
Futures Position
Short ITC Futures
@
450
10%
405
Gain on futures = 45 per share x 9600
$=^{+}432000$
On overall basis we were protected
Concept 2: Hedging a Stock - Using Index Futures
Suppose you hold 10,000 shares of Shalby hospitals which is currently trading @ 285. You expect an
adverse macro economic event to occur because of which share prices will fall, how can you protect yourself.
If stock futures on such stock are not traded then we use Index futures for heding, this is so because
there exists some connection between every stock & the index which is explained by ẞ
Interpretation of Beta ( )
ẞ tells us how the stock will move with respect to movements in the market. For example if  is 2 times, then it
means that for every 1% movement in index the share will move by 2% in the same direction.
EXAMPLE
Let us assume  of Shalby hospitals 1.5 times. Let us say Index is trading at 22000 with a lot
size of 50, how many Index Futures will you trade to hedge the position in spot?
Stock in Spot
Long $=7285\times10,000$ shares
$=\mp28,50,000$
Stock falls by @15%
Loss in Spot = 4,27,500
$\beta=1.5$ times
Since  Shalby hospitals is 1.5 times
Wow! Now we have achieved
complete hedging, since Loss in Spot
is Exactly Offset by Gain on Futures.
Incorrect Approach
Index Futures
Short in futures
$=728,50,000$
say, Index falls by @10%
Gain on Futures $=\mp2,85,000$
Oh No! It did not result in complete hedging
Correct Approach
Index Futures Short in futures
= $1.5~times\times28,50,000$
=  42,75,000
say↓ @10%
Gain on futures =

Concept 3: Hedging an entire Portfolio  by buying / selling share in spot
EXAMPLE
Q. Calculate  of portfolio
Interpretation -  of 1.365 times indicates that for every 1% fall in stock market our portfolio will fall by
1.365%.
How can we reduce ẞ, to 0.80?
!
Do not make the mistake of selectively selling one or two shares & selectively investing the
proceeds in specific shares since it will distort the composition of your portfolio.
Trick: We will sell all three stock in the same proportion as these are currently present in the
portfolio, consequently  of these three stocks combined together will remain same at 1.365.
But since the sale proceeds will be kept in cash / invested in Risk free having $\beta=0$, overall $B_{p}$ will
decrease.

DERIVATIVES ANALYSIS & VALUATION
Let the weight of combined stocks be X, hence weight of cash will be 1-X
$\beta_{p}=(\begin{matrix}\beta~of~combined&&Weight~of\\ stocks&comb~ined~stocks\end{matrix})+(\begin{matrix}\beta~of~cash&Weight~of\\ or~Rf&&cash~or~Rf\end{matrix})$
$0.80=1.365\times X+0\times(1-X)$
$0.80=1.365X$
$X=0.5861$
.. Amount to be kept in combined stocks
$=\mp46~lakhs\times0.5861=\mp26,96,060$

= 19,03,940
Action Portfolio manager should sell stocks worth 19,03,940 in the same proportion as these are present in
the Portfolio [14:20:12] and invest the proceeds in risk free security/keep in cash, in order to reduce  , to 0.80

Pay-off Graphs on Maturity Date
Gross Pay-off means Price difference exchanged between option buyer & seller on due date.
Net payoff means Gross pay off adjusted by premium amount
Net payoff of an option buyer = Gross pay off - Premium paid
Net pay off of an option seller = Premium received - Gross payoff

Arbitrage Prospects
DERIVATIVES ANALYSIS & VALUATION
Before Maturity Date
Put - Call Parity Theorem
$V_{s}+V_{p}=V_{c}+PV$ of Ex. Price
here, $V_{s}$ means value of stock i.e. So
V & V Value of Call/Put i.e. Call/Put Premium Today
EXAMPLE
ITC CMP = 285
3m Call option Ex. Price = 300 trading at a premium of 8
$R_{f}=7\%$ p.a.
Calc Price of 3m $POE\times P=\mp300$?
Solve:
$V_{S}+V_{P}=V_{C}+PV$ of Ex. P
$285+V_{p}=8+\frac{300}{(1+0.07\times3/12)}$
$\therefore V_{p}=\mp17.84$
hence, Fair $Vp=\mp17.84$
Derivation of Put - Call Parity Theorem
"If Two alternatives have same maturity value & same risk then their initial investment must also be the same"
It is evident from the above Table that Maturity CF's & risks of the two investment avenue are same. Hence,
their initial inv must also be the same.
Buying a Stock & Buying a PO
= Buying a CO & Inv in Requivalent to PV of Ex. P
$-V_{s}$
$-V_{p}$
=
$-v_{c}$
- PV of Ex. Price
Hence, $V_{s}+V_{p}=V_{c}+PV$ of Ex. P.
Two Assumptions before applying Put-Call party :-
Both CO & PO must have Same Exercise Price
Both CO & PO must have Same Maturity date
CA, CFA (USA), CPA (USA) PRAVEEN KHATOD - Leaders in Advanced Financial Education Across India

Q What if Actual $V_{p}=\overline{8}15$
Solve: Wow! Arbitrage opportunity
DERIVATIVES ANALYSIS & VALUATION
Trick: Buy one of the investment avenue (that entails lower outflow today) & sell other Investment
Avenue (that results in higher inflow today)
Since Actual $V_{p}$ (15) < fair V, (17.84), therefore, PO is Undervalued, Hence, an arbitrageur should:
(i)
Buy PO $ExP=\mp300$
(ii)
Buy in Spot
(iii)
Sell CO Ex. $P=\mp300$
(iv)
Borrow an amount equivalent to PV of Ex. P.
Sell R Inv.
to earn risk free arbitrage gain of 2.84 today.
Q What if Actual
$V_{p}=\overline{7}25$
Solve: Since Actual V, (25)> fair $V_{p}$ (17.84), therefore, PO is Overvalued, Hence, an arbitrageur should:
(i)
Sell PO $E\times P=\mp300$
(ii)
Sell in Spot
(iii)
Buy CO Ex. $P=\mp300$
(iv)
Invest an amount equivalent to PV of Ex. P.
to earn risk free arbitrage gain of 7.16 today.

$0.18=0.30P$
P
A
= 0.60 i.e. Prob of Rise

or
${}_{u}S_{1}\times P+{}_{d}S_{1}\times(1-P)=S_{0}\times(1+Rf)$

$360\times P+270\times(1-P)=300\times1.08$

$P=\frac{324-270}{360-270}$
.. $P=0.60$

$=_{u}V_{c}\times P+_{d}V_{c}\times(1-P)$
!
$=\not\equiv40\times0.60+\mathbb{F}0\times(1-0.6)$
= 24
Don't make the mistake of comparing $S_{0}$ & $S_{1}$ i.e. don't compare ₹300 & 360 and write 60 here.
Dude, here we have to write $V_{c}$ hence compare Ex. P vs $S_{1}$

$=\frac{7.24}{1.16}\frac{7.24}{1+0.16\times6/12}$
$=722.22$
Two Assumptions of risk neutral model
!

match with life of an option. Don't make the
mistake of dividing by 1.16 directly
✓ An Investor is neutral between R Investment & Investment in stock market as far as Risk is concerned.
✓ A Stock might assume only 2 possible prices on maturity date.

Two Period Binomial Model/ Multiple Period Binomial Model
applied when Price of Underlying Share changes more than once before maturity

Probability of Price Moving up i.e. $P=\frac{i-d}{u-d}$
(in 4 Decimals)
here,
$u=\frac{Expected~Price~of~underiying~Share~at1^{s\prime}Period(Move~up)}{Current~Price~of~underiying~share~at^{\prime}Time}\circ r\frac{\omega S_{1}}{S_{0}}$
$I=\frac{Expected~Price~of~underiying~Share~at~1st~Period(Move~Down)}{Current~Price~of~underiying~share~at^{\prime}Time}of~undering~share~at^{\prime}Time}or^{\prime}\frac{dS_{1}}{S_{0}}$
$i=1+Rf$ p.a. xt or et

Probability of Price Moving Down (in 4 Decimals) = 1 - P
$u=\frac{330}{300}=1.1$ $d=\frac{270}{300}=0.90$
$P=\frac{(1+0.16\times\frac{6}{12})-0.90}{1.1-0.90}=\frac{1.08-0.90}{1.1-0.90}=0.90$
$1-P=1-0.90=0.10$

Node D, E, F, G in our example, by comparing Spot Price at maturity vs. Exercise Price

Node $E=297-290=7$
Node $F=297-290=7$
Node $G=0$ [Lapse]

Step 2: Create a Perfectly hedged position
A perfectly hedged position can be created in either of
the following two ways: -
1. Buy 0.4444 shares & Sell 1 CO today or
2. Sell 0.4444 shares & Buy 1 CO today
Let's assume that we Buy 0.4444 Shares & Sell 1 CO today

DERIVATIVES ANALYSIS & VALUATION
Step 3: Calculate Maturity proceeds of guaranteed outcome
It may be observed that guaranteed outcome [M] is same @ 120 irrespective of stock price on
maturity date.
Step 4: PV of maturity proceeds and fair Ve Today
PV of Maturity Proceeds $w=\frac{-M}{1+r\times n/12}=\frac{-120}{1+0.16\times6/12}=-111.11$
Why Minus Sign?
Since we are receiving Inflow on Maturity date, hence, we would need to incur Outflow today so as to
receive Inflow on Maturity date.
A share $\times S_{0}+V_{c}$
= PV of maturity proceeds
. $V_{c}$ i.e. Fair $V_{c}=\mp22.22$
0.4444 share $\times\mp300+V_{c}=-111.111$
Q What if in above case Actual CO Premium is ruling @ 25
Solve:
A
!
There is NO need to apply 4 action arbitrage (taught earlier at the time of PC Parity Theorem.)
Instead we will use 3 action arbitrage [because there are only 2 possible prices on maturity date.
Conclusion: When only 2 possible prices on mat date (i.e. Risk neutral, The Binomial Model,
Perfectly hedged positions) - Use 3 action arbitrage
When more than 2 possible prices on mat date (eg., The black scholes model) - Use 4
action arbitrage
Since Actual V (25) > Fair V (22.22), CO is Overvalued. Hence we will:
(i) Sell 1 CO
(ii) Buy 0.4444 Share
(iii) Borrow an amount equivalent to PV of Maturity proceeds to earn risk free arbitrage gain of 2.78 today
Since action (i) & (ii) will result in Net Outflow hence we will Borrow the Amount.
Note: If Action (i) & (ii) will result in Net Inflow then we will Invest the Amount.

Q What is the expected rate of return on the above option if chances of above variations are 70% and 30%
respectively and CO can be bought today at 22.22?
Solve:
Expected Option Value at maturity $=(\mp360-\mp320)\times0.70+\mp0\times0.30=\mp28$
Expected Rate of Return on the Option
$=\frac{28-22.22}{22.22}\times100=26.02\%$

The Black-Scholes Model
DERIVATIVES ANALYSIS & VALUATION
Delta of a
Call Option
Risk neutral
prob. of exercise
i.e. hedge ratio
$V_{c}=S_{0}\times\sqrt{N(d_{1})}-\frac{E\times N(d_{2})}{e^{rr}}$
$d_{1}_{1}=\frac{Ln[S_{0}/E]+[r+0.5~\sigma^{2}]t}{\sigma\sqrt{t}}$
Step
Step 1
Step
here,
$d_{2}=\frac{Ln[S_{0}/E]+[r-0.5~\sigma^{2}]t}{\sigma\sqrt{t}}.$ or $d_{2}=d_{1}-\sigma\sqrt{t}$
$S_{0}$ Spot price today
E means Exercise price
r means risk-free rate p.a.
 means time remaining till maturity $[n/12$ or $n/365$
Ln means Log natural
$d_{1}$ & $d_{2}$
No. of deviations i.e. Z
Alternatively
$V_{c}=S_{o}\times N[d_{1}]-\frac{X\times N[d_{2}]}{e^{rt}}$
$d_{1}=\frac{Ln[S_{o}/X]+[r+\frac{variance}{2}]\dagger}{\sigma\sqrt{t}}$
$d_{2}=d_{1}-\sigma\sqrt{t}$
here,
X means Exercise price
Step2 $N[d_{1}]\&N[d_{2}]$ means Cumulative Area (under Normal Distribution Curve) upto $d_{1}$ & upto $d_{2}$
Note 1. In case of a dividend paying stock:
• If div amt is given in absolute terms → calc PV of Dividend & then deduct it from $S_{0},$
it will now become "Net $S_{0}^{\prime\prime}$ Use this Net $S_{0}$ everywhere in the formulas in place of $S_{0}$
• If div is given in yield% terms →
✓ Replacer by $(r-y)$ in $d_{1}(\&d_{2})$ formula
✓ Replace $S_{0}$ by i.e. PV of spot price discounted at div yield% in $V_{c}$ formulas
$\frac{S_{0}}{e^{yt}}$
only. Don't make this change in d₁ $d_{2}$ formula.
$V_{c}=\frac{S_{0}\times N[d_{1}]}{e^{\tau\tau}}-\frac{E\times N[d_{2}]}{e^{\tau\tau}}$
$d_{1}=\frac{Ln[S_{0}/E]+[(r-y)+0.5~\sigma^{2}]t}{\sigma\sqrt{t}}.$
$d_{2}=d_{1}-\sigma\sqrt{t}$
Note 2. To calc $V_{p}$
either Use Formula
$V_{p}=\frac{E\times[1-N(d_{2})]}{e^{rt}}-S_{0}\times[1-N(d_{1})].$
or Use below process
i)
First calc $V_{c}$ using above formula
ii)
Second apply Put-Call Parity theorem to find $V_{p}$
Hedging
If Long in Spot → then Buy Put option to hedge long exposure
If Short in Spot → then Buy Call option to hedge short exposure

Question 1
(8 Marks) Exam Dec 2021, May 2025
On 31/08/2021 Mr. R has taken a Long position of Two lots of Nifty Futures at 17300.
One lot of Nifty future is 50 units.
Initial Margin required is 10% of Contract Value.
Maintenance Margin required is 80% of Initial Margin.
The closing price of 5 days are given below-
You are required to-
(i)
Prepare a statement showing the daily balances in the margin account & payment on margin calls, if any.
(ii)
Compute the Gain or Loss of Mr. R, if contract squared off on 07/09/2021.
(iii) What would be the Gain or Loss if Mr. R, had taken the short position?
Solution:
(i)
Contract Size $(=17,300\times50\times2)$
= 17,30,000
Initial Margin (10% of 17,30,000)
= 1,73,000
Maintenance Margin (80% of 1,73,000) = 1,38,400
Statement showing the daily balances in Margin $A/c$ and margin call if any,
(ii) Gain or Loss of Mr. R squared off position on 07/09/21

Question 2
Study Material, (5 Marks) Exam May 2012
On 31-8-2011, the value of stock index was
dividend yield on this Stock Index is as under:
2200. The risk free rate of return has been 8% per annum. The
Assuming that interest is continuously compounded, find out the future price of contract deliverable on 31-
0.01583
12-2011. Given e
$=1.01593$
Solution: The price of futures, when dividend yield is given, is written as:
$F=Se^{(r-d)\times t}$
here
$F=?$ $S=2200$ $r=8\%$ or 0.08;
$d=$ Average dividend yield of four months viz. September to December
$=(3+3+4+3)/4=3.25\%$ or 0.0325
$t=$ Time to expiry $=4$ months or $4/12$ or 0.333
$F=2200\times e$ (0.08-0.0325)×0.333 $=2200\times e$
$=2200\times1.01593=2235.046$
0.01583

Question 3
DERIVATIVES ANALYSIS & VALUATION
Study Material, RTP May 2022, (8 Marks) Exam July 2021, MTP Sep 2022
We assume that a futures contract on the BSE index with four months maturity is used to hedge the value of
portfolio over next three months. One future contract is for delivery of 50 times the index.

Question 5
(5 Marks) Exam May 2012, RTP Nov 21, RTP Nov 2023, Sep 2025
A company is long on 10 MT of copper @ 534 per kg (spot) and intends to remain so for the ensuing quarter.
The variance of change in its spot and future prices are 16% and 36% respectively, having correlation
coefficient of 0.75. The contract size of one contract is 1,000 kgs.
Required:
(i)
Calculate the Optimal Hedge Ratio for perfect hedging in Future Market.
(ii) Advice the position to be taken in Future Market for perfect hedging.
(iii) Determine the number and the amount of the copper futures to achieve a perfect hedge.
Solution:
(i)
(ii)
The optional hedge ratio to minimize the variance of Hedger's position is given by:
$H=\rho\frac{\sigma_{S}}{\sigma_{F}}$
$\sigma_{s}=$
Standard deviation of $\Delta S$ (Change in Spot Prices)
$\sigma_{F}=$ Standard deviation of $\Delta F$ (Change in Future Prices)
$\rho=$ coefficient of correlation between $\Delta S$ and $\Delta F$
$H=$ Hedge Ratio
$\Delta S=$ change in Spot price.
$\Delta F=$ change in Future price.
Accordingly
Standard deviation of $\Delta S=v}16\%=4\%$ and
Standard deviation of $\Delta F=\sqrt{}36\%=6\%$ and
$H=0.75\times\frac{0.04}{0.06}=0.5$
Since the company is long position in Spot (Cash) Market it shall take Short Position in Future Market.
(iii) Since contact size of one contract is 1,000 Kg,
No. of contract to be short =
10,000 Kgs
1,000 kgs
 0.50 = 5 Contracts
Amount $=5000\times\times534=\overline{\times}26,70,000$

contracts

$=\mathbb{Z}2,20,000-\mathbb{Z}2,00,000+\mathbb{Z}70,000$
= 90,000

Study Material, (5 Marks) Exam May 2011, MTP May 2025
A Mutual Fund is holding the following assets in Crores:
The Beta of the equity shares portfolio is 1.1. The index future is selling at 4300 level. The Fund Manager
apprehends that the index will fall at the most by 10%. How many index futures he should short for perfect
hedging? One index future consists of 50 units.
Substantiate your answer assuming the Fund Manager's apprehension will materialize.
CA, CFA (USA), CPA (USA) PRAVEEN KHATOD - Leaders in Advanced Financial Education Across India
256
Alpha Academy
DERIVATIVES ANALYSIS & VALUATION
Solution: Number of index future to be sold by the Fund Manager is:
$\frac{1.1\times90,00,0000}{4,300\times50}=4,605$
Justification of the answer:
Loss in the value of the portfolio if the index falls by 10% is $\mathbb{7}\frac{11}{100}\times90~crore=\mathbb{7}9.90~Crore$ .
Gain by short covering of index future is: $\frac{0.1\times4,300\times50\times4,605}{1,00,00,000}=9.90~Crore$
This justifies the answer. Further, cash is not a part of the portfolio.

Question 15
Study Material, (8 Marks) Exam May 2012
Sumana wanted to buy shares of EIL which has a range of 411 to 592 a month later. The present price per
share is 421. Her broker informs her that the price of this share can sore up to 522 within a month or so, so
that she should buy a one month CALL of EIL. In order to be prudent in buying the call, the share price should
be more than or at least 522 the assurance of which could not be given by her broker.
Though she understands the uncertainty of the market, she wants to know the probability of attaining the
share price 592 so that buying of a one month CALL of EIL at the execution price of 522 is justified. Advise
0.036
her. Take the risk free interest to be 3.60% and e
$=1.037$
Solution:
$p=\frac{e^{\tau}-d}{u-d}$
$e^{rt}=e^{0.036}$ $d=411/421=0.976$; $u=592/421=1.406$
$P=\frac{e^{0.036}-0.976}{1.406-0.976}=\frac{1.037-0.976}{0.43}=\frac{0.061}{0.43}=0.1418.$
Thus Probability of Rise in Price to 0.1418

The composition of the implied risk-less hedge portfolio at valuation date is called Delta ( ) and it is calculated
as follows:
$\frac{C_{u}-C_{o}}{S_{u}-S_{d}}$
Where,
$C_{u}=$ Pay-off from Call Option if price of Stock goes up
$C_{d}=$ Pay-off from Call Option if price of Stock goes down
$S_{u}=$
Upward price of the Stock
$S_{d}=$ Downward price of the Stock

shall be computed as follows:
$\Delta=\frac{5-0}{33-27}=\frac{5}{6}$
Thus, $\frac{5}{6}$
shares shall be held or purchased for writing one Call Option.

or

Solution:
WN# 1 Calc pv of dividend
$=\frac{\overline{7}5.20}{e^{0.12\times4/12}}=\frac{\overline{7}5.20}{1.04081}=\overline{7}5$
Applying the Black Scholes Formula,
Value of the Call option now:
... Net $S_{0}=\overline{7}85-\overline{7}5=\overline{7}80$
$C=S\times N(d_{1})-k\times e^{-rt}N(d_{2})$
$d_{1}=\frac{Ln(s/k)+(r+\sigma^{2}/2)t}{\sigma\sqrt{t}}$
$d_{2}=d_{2}-\sigma\sqrt{t}$
$d_{1}=\frac{Ln(1.0667)+(0.12+(0.08))0.5}{0.40\sqrt{0.5}}$
$=\frac{0.0645+(0.2)0.5}{0.40\times0.7071}=0.5820$
$d_{2}=0.5820-0.2828=0.2992$
$Nd_{1}=N(0.5820)$
$Nd_{2}=N(0.2992)$
$=0.6177$
Where,
$C=$ Theoretical call premium
$S=$
Current stock price
$t=$ time until option expiration

Efficient Market Hypothesis | Efficient Market Theory
developed by
Eugen Fama
As per Efficient Market Hypothesis, all available price sensitive information is fully reflected in
securities prices i.e. no one can beat the market. It is impossible to outperform the overall market
because stocks are always traded at their fair value.

Test of Weak form Efficiency
TECHNICAL ANALYSIS
(4 Marks) Exam May 2025
Three ways to test weak form of efficiency (1) Run Test (2) Auto/ Serial Correlation (3) Filter Rules Test
Run Test
Given a series of stock price changes each price change is designated + if it represents an increase and
- if it represents a decrease. The resulting series may be like -,+
A run occurs when there is no difference between the sign of two changes. When the sign of change
differs, the run ends and new run begins. Below are the Steps in Run Test
Step 1: Assign +/- sign to the closing prices.
Tutorial Note:
'+' is assigned if stock prices has increased today
'-' is assigned if stock prices has decreased today
1.
Step 2: Count
$n_{1}$, $n_{2}$ & r
2.
(i)
$n_{1}=$
No. of Positive changes
(ii)
$n_{2}=$ No. of Negative changes
(iii) $r=$ No. of runs or No. of sign changes (eg.
If Q gives open Price, High Price, Low
Prices & Closing Prices then consider
Closing Prices for assigning +/- sign
Price on the 1st day is not assigned any sign
(leave it blank, don't even put "-" dash else
it will confuse with "-" minus sign.)
runs)
02
Step 3: Calculate average no. of runs $(\mu_{r})$
$\mu_{r}=\frac{2n_{1}n_{2}}{n_{1}+n_{2}}+1$
$\hat{\phi}=\sqrt{\frac{2n_{1}n_{2}(2n_{1}n_{2}-n_{1}-n_{2})}{(n_{1}+n_{2})^{2}(n_{1}+n_{2}-1)}}$
Step 4: Calculate Standard Deviation
As Per ICAI study material
Alternatively,
$\hat{\phi}=\sqrt{\frac{(\mu-1)(\mu-2)}{(n_{1}+n_{2}-1)}}$
Step 5: Calculate lower limit & upper limit
Lower limit $=\mu-t\times\hat{\sigma}$ or $\mu-t\times\sigma$ Upper limit $=\mu+t\times\hat{\sigma}$ or $\mu+t\times\sigma$
1. Value of t at a specific level of significance & at a specific degree of freedom is either
For a sample of size n, the t-distribution will have n-1 degrees of freedom.
given in the Q or found using T- table
2.
Level of significance is just like 'VAR under normal distribution curve'.
3.
In our case, sample size is $n_{1}+n_{2}$ hence $df=n_{1}+n_{2}-1.$
Step 6: Decision
If 'r' lies between lower, & upper limit then market exhibits weak form of efficiency.
If 'r' lies outside the range then markets are inefficient.
Step2 Calc r (No. of times sign changes)
Step 3 Avg (μ)

$\mu+t\times\sigma$

Alpha Academy
Auto Correlation / Serial Correlation
TECHNICAL ANALYSIS
means Correlation of a given time series with a lagged version of itself. It measures relationship b/w
current stock prices and its own past stock prices.
Steps to calc Auto Correlation
Step 1: Divide the given series of prices into 2 equal series eg. if 10 days prices are given then first 5
prices becomes first series, last 5 prices becomes second series
Step 2: Calculate changes in prices in {Prefer if Q is silent} or in% terms as compared to previous price
for both the series
$\Delta$ in price in first series is named as 'X' variable
$\Delta$ in price in second series is named as 'Y' variable
Step 3: Now calc correlation between X & Y
Step 4: Conclusion:
If correlation is weak (say b/w - 0.30 to + 0.30) then it is not possible to predict the prices
using Technical analysis & hence market exhibits weak form of efficiency
If correlation is moderate or strong +ve / -ve then markets are inefficient
Filter Rules Test
✓ If the price of stock increases by at least N% buy and hold it.
✓ Sell the stock when the price decreases at least N% from a subsequent high.
If the behaviour of stock price changes is random, filter rules should not apply in such a buy and hold
strategy. By and large, studies suggest that filter rules do not outperform a single buy and hold
strategy particularly after considering commission on transaction.
Challenges to the Efficient Market Theory
RTP Jan 2026
(a) Information Inadequacy Information is neither freely available nor rapidly transmitted to all
participants in the stock market. There is a calculated attempt by many companies to circulate
misinformation.
(b) Limited information processing capabilities Human information processing capabilities are sharply
limited.
(c) Irrational Behaviour It is generally believed that investor's rationality will ensure a close
correspondence between market prices and intrinsic values. The market seems to function largely
on hit miss tactics rather then on basis of informed beliefs about the long term prospects of
individual enterprises.
(d) Monopolistic Influence In practice, powerful institutions and big operators wield great influence
over the market.
Misconception about Efficient Market Theory
Although price tends to fluctuate they cannot reflect fair value. This is because the future is
uncertain. The market springs surprises continually and as prices reflect the surprises they fluctuate.
The random movement of stock prices suggests that stock market is irrational. Randomness and
irrationality are two different things, if investors are rational and competitive, price changes are
bound to be random.
CA, CFA (USA), CPA (USA) PRAVEEN KHATOD - Best Faculty in India for Financial Management Courses

Study Material, RTP Nov 2023, MTP Jan 2026
The closing value of Sensex for the month of October, 2017 is given below:
Alpha Academy
TECHNICAL ANALYSIS
You are required to test the weak form of efficient market hypothesis by applying the run test at 5% and 10%
level of significance.
Following value can be used:
Value of t at 5% is 2.101 at 18 degrees of freedom
Value of t at 10% is 1.734 at 18 degrees of freedom
Value of t at 5% is 2.086 at 20 degrees of freedom.
Value of t at 10% is 1.725 at 20 degrees of freedom.
Solve:
Total of sign of price changes $(r)=8$
No of Positive changes $=n_{1}=11$
No. of Negative changes $=n_{2}=8$
$\mu_{r}=\frac{2n_{1}n_{2}}{n_{1}+n_{2}}+1$
$\mu_{r}=\frac{2\times11\times8}{11+8}+1=\frac{176}{19}+1=10.26$
$\underline{\phi}=\frac{2n_{1}n_{2}(2n_{1}n_{2}-n_{1}-n_{2})}{(n_{1}+n_{2})^{2}(n_{1}+n_{2}-1)}$
$\underline{\phi}=\frac{(2\times11\times8)(2\times11\times8-11-8)}{(11+8)^{2}(11+8-1)}$
$=\frac{176\times157}{(19)^{2}(18)}=4.252=2.06$
Since too few runs in the case would indicate that the movement of prices is not random. We employ a two-
tailed test the randomness of prices.
Test at 5% level of significance at 18 degrees of freedom using t- table
The lower limit
$=\mu-t\times\hat{\sigma}=10.26-2.101\times2.06=5.932$
At 10% level of significance at 18 degrees of freedom
Lower limit
$=10.26-1.734\times2.06=6.688$
Upper limit
$=\mu+t\times\hat{\sigma}=10.26+2.101\times2.06=14.588$
Upper limit
$=10.26+1.734\times2.06=13.832$
As seen r lies between these limits. Hence, the market exhibits weak form of efficiency.
*For a sample of size n, the t distribution will have n-1 degrees of freedom.

Types of Rates
Spot rate
FOREIGN EXCHANGE EXPOSURE & RISK MANAGEMENT
This rate is for immediate settlement. However,
practically spot rate means $T+2$ settlement
Forward rate
This rate is agreed upon today for
settlement on some future date.
PIPS [Price interest point or Percentage in point]
If Q is silent then Currency Forward
contracts are always settled by actual
delivery & not by price difference
PIPS is the smallest unit by which a currency quotation can change. Since most of international
quotations are upto 4 decimal places, therefore, minimum change is 0.0001. Now this change of 0.0001
will be called as change by 1 Pips.
$1~Pips=0.0001$
$f~1=\$1.1123$
Price has changed by 4 pips
\$1 = 84.5050-84.5175
Spread is 125 pips
$f1=\$1.1127$
Swap Points [aka Forward points, Forward margin or Premium on forward contract]
Swap Points are the difference between spot rate & forward rate.
EXAMPLE
1 m Forward $\$1=786.5125-86.5250$
Spot
\$1=86.4950 86.5000
Swap points 175
250
Increasing Order
Rules for adjustment of swap points:
1. If swap points are in increasing order then add swap points to spot rate
2. If swap points are in decreasing order then deduct swap points from spot rate
=
\$ 1.1110 1.1250
80
40

\$ 1.1030 1.1210

Telephone format is used for rates at
the same point of time and are based
on the concept of 'Replacement'
Swap points are used for
rates at two different point
of time and are based on
the concept of 'Add / less'

Broken Period Forward Contract
Interbank Forward Rates are for Standard due dates whereas a Customer can approach Bank to
enter into a forward Contract for some Non-Standard due dates. In such cases' the swap Points
applicable for Standard due dates falling immediately before & immediately after non-standard due
dates are interpolated.

$=\frac{88-80}{80}\times100\times\frac{12}{12}$
$=+10\%i.e.10\%$ app. in \$

5. A General Note regarding mistake by ICAI in case of app/ dep% given
Say, \$1 = 80
If ICAI says \$ (LHS Currency) is appreciating by 10%, then $\$1=\mp88$ (& this is correct)
If ICAI says (RHS Currency) is depreciating by 10%, then ICAI assumes that depn = \$app, hence
they assume that \$ is app by 10% and write the same answer $\$1=\mp88$ [Ideally it should be 88.88, but
ICAI doesn't do so in many questions, specially in IFM chapter]
Conclusion: The Rule ICAI is following is (specially for IFM Chapter)
If %app is given on LHS Currency then add app% on RHS Currency value (this is conceptually correct)
If %app is given on RHS Currency then they assume that LHS Currency is dep by same% (which is
conceptually incorrect, but ICAI does so) and now deduct dep% on RHS currency value.
Export import date
i.e $10^{th}$ feb 26

\$1 = 81
Transaction Risk: Change in expected Cash flows arising between the Transaction date & Actual Cash
flow Receipt/Payment date due to an unexpected change in exchange rates.
Translation Exposure: arises due to translation of Foreign Currency assets or liabilities into the home
currency.
Economic Exposure: refers to an extent to which economic value of a company can decline due to
changes in exchange rate. Changes in exchange rates can impact firm's cost of input, prices of its
outputs and its competitive position leading to a change in demand of product. Economic/ Operating
exposure is calculated as Gain/ (Loss) due to Increase/ Decrease in demand at settlement date
exchange rate.
Political Risk: when a country's government unexpectedly changes its policies e.g. trade barriers.
Note: If a company agrees to Forward Contract Rate which is less beneficial as compared to Today's
Spot rate, then the difference between Forward Rate Vs. Spot Rate can also be termed as 'Probable
Loss of Operating Profit' due to Transaction Exposure.

FOREIGN EXCHANGE EXPOSURE & RISK MANAGEMENT
Techniques of Risk Management
☐
☐
☐
☑
Do Nothing
It means not taking any kind of hedging cover on the assumption that movement in exchange rates will
sometimes be adverse & sometimes favourable, offsetting each other over a period of time.
Home Currency Invoicing
It means resorting to generating/ receiving invoices in Home Currency. Eg. Indian firms start
invoicing in terms.
Leading & Lagging
is a decision made by comparing Inflow/ Outflow under two situations:-
(i) If we Lead (pay/ receive early) vs.
(ii) If we Lag (delay the payment/receipt)
Trick for comparison Bring outcome of both the alternative at the same point of time, say at the end
of 3m or 6 months.
Alpha Academy
FOREIGN EXCHANGE EXPOSURE & RISK MANAGEMENT
Whether to use @ Borrowing rate % or @ Investment rate% to add interest ?
Generally, we use Borrowing rate % for an Importer. However, if Q mentions that an importer is
running Cash surplus then Inv. Rate % being opportunity cost is relevant
In case of an exporter, generally we use investment rate % However, if Q mentions that an exporter
has Loan Outstanding then borrowing Rate % being intt. saved becomes relevant.
Exposure Netting
Exposure netting involves squaring-off Import exposure Vs. Export exposure & pay / receive
only the net amount.
Bilateral Netting
Two types of exposure netting
Multilateral Netting
Two companies are involved
Bilateral Netting
More than 2 companies (usually
from the same group) are involved

Multilateral Netting
This process is generally adopted among two or more subsidiaries in the same group. Steps involved are:
Step 1: Decide a Common Currency. It would usually be headquarter's currency
Step 2: Convert all O/s exposure in a common currency as decided above & write in the Netting Matrix & solve it
Step 3: Summarize above Matrix & calculate Net Payment/Receipt

FOREIGN EXCHANGE EXPOSURE & RISK MANAGEMENT
A group of companies is controlled from the USA. This group has subsidiaries in UK,
Euroland and Japan. For convenience, these are referred to as UK, EL and JP. As on 31st
March, inter-company indebtedness stood as under:

US $\phi1=\epsilon0.90$; Sterling 0.70; ¥ 120.

subsidiaries, after netting off.
Conclusion Table
Amount in \$ millions
Matching
Answer: UK pays \$ 259.53 mn, EL receives \$192.86 mn, JP receives \$66.67 mn
Matching is a mechanism whereby a company matches its foreign currency inflows with its foreign
currency outflows in respect of amount and approximate timing.
Natural matching-> Receipts in a particular currency are used to make payments in that same foreign
currency thereby reducing the need for a group of companies to go through the foreign exchange
markets to the unmatched portion of foreign currency cash flows.
Parallel matching -> in which the matching is achieved with receipt and payment in different currencies
but these currencies are expected to move closely together, near enough in parallel.
Price Variation
Price variation involves increasing selling prices to counter the adverse effects of exchange rate change.
Asset and Liability Management
This technique can be used to manage balance sheet, income statement or cash flow exposures.
Aggressive postures -> the firm simply increases exposed cash inflows denominated in currencies
expected to be strong or increases exposed cash outflows denominated in weak currencies.
Defensive postures-> matching cash inflows and outflows according to their currency of denomination,
irrespective of whether they are in strong or weak currencies.
CA, CFA (USA), CPA (USA) PRAVEEN KHATOD - Leaders in Advanced Financial Education Across India

Standard Comment: In either case, decision to take Forward Cover was justified. This is so
because decision was taken on some prior date when the actual spot rates on due date were
not known. No CFO can predict with certainty as to what would be the exchange rate on some
future date. Forward Cover provides one way protection & the justification of decision lies in
that protection. It will be wrong to question the correctness of decision on hind-sight basis.

Extension of Forward Contract
it can be decomposed into 2 parts
(1) Cancellation of original contract (as per concepts taught in case of cancellation)
(2) Entering into a fresh forward contract with new maturity date

Step 2: Evaluate arbitrage opportunity
If actual forward rate  fair forward rate then it will give rise to arbitrage opportunities
How to identify direction of arbitrage [ie. from which country to borrow & in which country to invest]
As done by ICAI -
Compare,
Interest rate differential
Both rh & rf must be for
the same period as the
period of forward contract
Derivation of above formula
=
$B^{rh-rf}=$
Exchange rate differential
% Prem/ (disc) on LHS currency based on actual
forward rates & spot rates
$\frac{1+rh}{1+rf}=\frac{F_{1}&Sub+racting1~fro\\ S_{o}&\frac{1+rh}{1+rf}-1=\frac{F_{1}}{S_{o}}-1$
both the sides
This is Actual
Forward Rate (NOT
fair forward rate)
on LHS
currency
$\frac{1^{\prime}+rh-T-rf}{1+rf}=\frac{F_{1}-S_{0}}{S_{0}}\frac{rh-rf}{-1+rf}=\%App/(dep)}ci$
Ignored as it doesn't have a big effect
If interest rate differential = Exchange rate differential, the NO arbitrage opp
If interest rate differential  Exchange rate differential, the NO arbitrage opp exists
In our example,
rh-rf
=
i.e. intt rate differential
% app/(dep) on LHS currency
i.e. exchange rate differential
$8\%-4\%=\frac{82-80}{80}$
+4%
+2.5%
Since Exchange rate differential < Intt Rate Differential, therefore, Arbitrage opp exists. An arbitrageur
should Borrow in \$ & invest in to earn risk free arbitrage gain.
Tutorial Note:
An easy way to find the correct direction of arbitrage is here.
Use Trial & Error method - Simply assume Borrowing some amount from any one of
the country & invest in other country. Now run the arbitrage on calculator.
✓ If it results in gain then above direction is correct.
✓ If it results in loss then opposite direction is correct.

Overlapping Exchange Rates / Two-Point Arbitrage / Geographical Arbitrage
HDFC Bank
BANK
$\$1=\mp83.40-83.80$
ICICI Bank
BANK
SBI
₹
$\$1=\mp83.25-83.70$
Oh wow! Exchange Rates are
different between HDFC bank
& SBI. Let's Arbitrage......
So Sorry! there's NO Arbitrage opportunity
between HDFC bank and SBI
$\$1=\mp84.50-84.55$
But Yes! Arbitrage Opp exists now between SBI & ICICI!
Despite different Exchange rates being quoted by various Banks still these rates are so arranged that
BID Rates of All the Banks < Lowest Ask Rate
Ask Rates of All the Banks > Highest of the Bid Rate
In other words, Highest Bid Rate < Lowest Ask Rate
If it is NOT so then Arbitrage opportunities exists!
Steps in Arbitrage
1.
2.
3.
Find Lowest Ask Rate among all the Banks quotations.
Find Highest Bid Rate among all the Quotations.
Check whether
Highest Bid Rate < Lowest Ask Rate
No arbitrage opportunity exits
if so then Arbitrage Opportunity doesn't exist.
if not so then Buy LHS currency @Lowest Ask Rate & Sell LHS Currency @ Highest Bid Rate.

Relative form

Spot

Taxes.

International Fisher Effect
Nominal Interest Rates contains (i) a real rate of return and (ii) anticipated Inflation. If investors
across all countries require same real return, the nominal interest rate differentials between any two
countries may be the result of differential in expected inflation rates only.
Basic Concept
(1 + Nominal Interest Rate) = (1 + Inflation Rate) (1 + Real Intt Rate)
$.07=1.05(1+Real~Intt)$
... Real Intt Rate = 1.905%~1.91%
Proof of International Fisher Effect
$\frac{(1+rh)}{(1+rf)}=\frac{(1+Ih)(1+RRh)}{(1+If)(1+RRf)}$
Since Real interest rate across the world will be same hence
$\frac{(1+rh)}{(1+rf)}=\frac{(1+Ih)}{(1+If)}$
it can now be observed that Differences in Interest Rates between any two countries is purely
because of differences in Inflation Rates
Nostro, Vostro & Loro Account
NOSTRO
"Our Account With you"
LORO ACCOUNT
"Their Account with them"
Eg. ICICI Bank 's $A/c$ with BOA
VOSTRO
"Your Account With us"
Eg. SBI's $A/c$ with Bank of America
Eg. BOA's $A/c$ with SBI
Exchange Position
Cash Position
Accounting in Nostro $A/c$
{It is just like Accrual $A/c\}$
{It is just like Receipt & Pymnt A/c}
1. If Open Position Overbought is given then write Op Bal of Exchange position on 'Net Purchases' side.
2. If Balance in Nostro $A/c$ Credit is given then write Op Bal of Cash position on 'Net Receipts' side
3. If Q gives some requirement to maintain some Closing balances then -
To maintain credit balance in Nostro $A/c$ - An appropriate amt should be Purchase/Sell in Spot.
[Important: Remember to give effect of your Spot Action in Exchange position as well]
To maintain Overbought position - An appropriate amt should be Purchase/ Sell in Forward.

(1)
You are required to calculate loss/gain due to transaction exposure.
(2)

exposure if the contracted price of air conditioners is 25,000:
(i)
the current exchange rate changes to
/Euro
51.75/80
/S\$
27.10/15
(ii)
Price elasticity of demand is estimated to be 1.5
(iii)
Payments and receipts are to be settled at the end of six months.
Solution:
(1) Profit at current exchange rates
$2400~units\times[E~500\times\vec{\times}51.50-(SS800\times\vec{\times}27.25+\vec{\times}1,000+\vec{\times}1,500)]$
$2400~units\times[\vec{\times}25,750-\vec{\times}24,300]=\vec{\times}34,80,000$
Profit after change in exchange rates
$2400~units\times[E~500\times\vec{\times}52-(SS800\times\vec{\times}27.75+\vec{\times}1000+\vec{\times}1500)]$
$2400~units\times[\vec{\times}26,000-\vec{\times}24,700]=\vec{\times}31,20,000$
LOSS DUE TO TRANSACTION EXPOSURE
34,80,000- 31,20,000 = 3,60,000
(2) Profit based on new exchange rates
$2400~units\times[\vec{\times}25,000-(SS800\times\vec{\times}27.15+\vec{\times}1,000+\vec{\times}1,500)]$
$2400~units\times[\vec{\times}25,000-\vec{\times}24,220]=\vec{\times}18,72,000$
Profit after change in exchange rates at the end of six months
$2400~units\times[\vec{z}25,000-(SS800\times\vec{z}27.75+\vec{z}1,000+\vec{z}1,500)]$
$2400~units\times[\vec{\times}25,000-\vec{\times}24,700]=\vec{\times}7,20,000$
DECLINE IN PROFIT DUE TO TRANSACTION EXPOSURE
18,72,000-7,20,000 = 11,52,000
Current price of each unit is $\mathcal{E}=\frac{\overline{7}25,000}{\overline{7}51.50}\mathcal{E}=485.44.$
Price after change in exch. rate $e=\frac{\overline{7}25,000}{\overline{7}51.75}E=483.09$
Change in Price due to change in Exch. Rate
€485.44 €483.09 = €2.35
$r(-)0.48\%$
Price elasticity of demand $=1.5$
Increase in demand due to fall in price $0.48\times1.5=0.72\%$
Size of increased order $=2400\times1.0072=2417~units$
Profit
$=2417[\vec{\times}25,000-(SS800\times\vec{\times}27.75+\vec{\times}1,000+\vec{\times}1,500)]$
Therefore, decrease in profit due to operating exposure
18,72,000-7,25,100 = 11,46,900
$=2417[\vec{\times}25,000-\vec{\times}24,700]=\vec{\times}7,25,100$

FOREIGN EXCHANGE EXPOSURE & RISK MANAGEMENT
Amount realized on selling Danish Kroner 10,00,000 at 6.5150 per Kroner = 65,15,000.
Cover at London:
Bank buys Danish Kroner at London at the market selling rate.
Pound sterling required for the purchase (DKK 10,00,000 ÷ DKK 11.4200) = GBP 87,565.67 Bank buys locally
GBP 87,565.67 for the above purchase at the market selling rate of 74.3200.
Cover at New York:
Bank buys Kroners at New York at the market selling rate.
Dollars required for the purchase of Danish Kroner ( $DKK10,00,000/7.5670)$
$=USD~1,32,152.77$
Bank buys locally USD 1,32,152.77 for the above purchase at the market selling rate of 49.2625.
The transaction would be covered through London which gets the maximum profit of 4,619 or lower cover
cost at London Market by 2,295
Tutorial Note: If Q also asks to calc cover rate then simply apply the concept of cross currency rates to
calc cover rate. Hint cover rate in London
& Cover rate in $NY=\mathbb{7}49.2625\times\frac{1}{7.5670}=\mathbb{7}6.5102$
$=\boxed{7}74.32\times\frac{1}{11.42}=\boxed{7}6.5079$
